**Kuwait**,[^1] officially the **State of Kuwait**,[^2] is a country in [West Asia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/West_Asia "West Asia"). With a coastline of approximately 500 km (311 mi), it is situated at the head of the [Persian Gulf](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persian_Gulf "Persian Gulf") in the northeastern edge of the [Arabian Peninsula](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arabian_Peninsula "Arabian Peninsula"), bordering [Iraq](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Iraq "Iraq") to [the north](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Iraq%E2%80%93Kuwait_border "Iraq–Kuwait border") and [Saudi Arabia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Saudi_Arabia "Saudi Arabia") to [the south](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kuwait%E2%80%93Saudi_Arabia_border "Kuwait–Saudi Arabia border").[^18] Kuwait is geographically the closest Gulf country to [mainland Iran](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Iranian_plateau "Iranian plateau") (separated only by a small [Iraqi coastline](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Al-Faw_peninsula "Al-Faw peninsula")).[^19] The country is a small [city-state](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/City-state "City-state");[^20] most of the population reside in the [urban agglomeration](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Urban_area "Urban area") of [Kuwait City](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kuwait_City "Kuwait City"), the capital and largest city.[^21] As of 2024, Kuwait has a population of 4.82 million, of which 1.53 million are [Kuwaiti citizens](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kuwaiti_nationality_law "Kuwaiti nationality law") while the remaining 3.29 million are [foreign nationals](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Expatriates_in_Kuwait "Expatriates in Kuwait") from over 100 countries.[^22] In 2024, Kuwait had the world's seventh [largest number of foreign nationals as a percentage of the population](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_sovereign_states_by_immigrant_and_emigrant_population "List of sovereign states by immigrant and emigrant population"), where its citizens make up fewer than 30% of the overall population.[^23]

The territory of modern-day Kuwait has been inhabited by humans since antiquity, particularly due to its strategic location near the mouth of the [Tigris and Euphrates rivers](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tigris%E2%80%93Euphrates_river_system "Tigris–Euphrates river system"). In the early 18th century, the territory of modern-day Kuwait was under the jurisdiction of the [Bani Khalid](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bani_Khalid_Emirate "Bani Khalid Emirate") clan; then the territory became known as the [Sheikdom of Kuwait](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sheikdom_of_Kuwait "Sheikdom of Kuwait") in 1752 and a [British](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/British_Empire "British Empire") [protectorate](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Anglo-Kuwaiti_Agreement_of_1899 "Anglo-Kuwaiti Agreement of 1899") in 1899. Prior to the [discovery of oil reserves](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Oil_reserves_in_Kuwait "Oil reserves in Kuwait") in 1938, the territory of modern-day Kuwait contained a regional trade port.[^24] [^25] The protectorate agreements with the United Kingdom ended in June 1961 when [Kuwait officially became an independent state](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/National_Day_\(Kuwait\) "National Day (Kuwait)").

From 1946 to 1982, Kuwait underwent large-scale modernization, largely based on income from [oil production](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Petroleum_industry_in_Kuwait "Petroleum industry in Kuwait"). In the 1980s, Kuwait experienced a period of geopolitical instability and an economic crisis following the [stock market crash](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Souk_Al-Manakh_stock_market_crash "Souk Al-Manakh stock market crash"). It suffered pro-Iranian attacks during the [Iran–Iraq War](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Iran%E2%80%93Iraq_War "Iran–Iraq War"), as a result of Kuwait's financial support to Iraq. In 1990, the state of Kuwait was [invaded](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Iraqi_invasion_of_Kuwait "Iraqi invasion of Kuwait"), had a [puppet regime](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Republic_of_Kuwait "Republic of Kuwait") installed, and was subsequently annexed by [Ba'athist Iraq](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ba%27athist_Iraq "Ba'athist Iraq") under the leadership of [Saddam Hussein](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Saddam_Hussein "Saddam Hussein") following disputes over oil production. The [Iraqi occupation of Kuwait](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kuwait_Governorate "Kuwait Governorate") ended on 26 February 1991, after a U.S.–led [international coalition](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Coalition_of_the_Gulf_War "Coalition of the Gulf War") expelled Iraqi forces from the country during the [Gulf War](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gulf_War "Gulf War").[^26]

Kuwait is a [high-income economy](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/World_Bank_high-income_economy "World Bank high-income economy"), backed by the world's [sixth largest oil reserves](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_countries_by_proven_oil_reserves#Countries "List of countries by proven oil reserves"). Like most other [Arab states of the Persian Gulf](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arab_states_of_the_Persian_Gulf "Arab states of the Persian Gulf"), it is an [emirate](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Emirate "Emirate"); the [emir](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Emir_of_Kuwait "Emir of Kuwait") is the head of state and the ruling [Al Sabah](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Al_Sabah "Al Sabah") family dominates the country's political system. Its official state religion is Islam, specifically the [Maliki school](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Maliki_school "Maliki school") of Sunni Islam. It is a founding member of the [Gulf Cooperation Council](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gulf_Cooperation_Council "Gulf Cooperation Council") (GCC) and is also a member of the [United Nations](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_Nations "United Nations"), [OPEC](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/OPEC "OPEC"), the [Arab League](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arab_League "Arab League"), and the [Organisation of Islamic Cooperation](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Organisation_of_Islamic_Cooperation "Organisation of Islamic Cooperation"). As of February 2026, Kuwait has the world's most valuable [currency](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Currency "Currency"), with one [Kuwaiti Dinar](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kuwaiti_dinar "Kuwaiti dinar") being worth 3.25 [USD](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States_dollar "United States dollar").[^27]

## Etymology

The name "Kuwait" is from the [Mesopotamian Arabic](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mesopotamian_Arabic "Mesopotamian Arabic") diminutive form of كويت (*Kut* or *Kout*), meaning "fortress built near water".[^28] The country's official name has been the "State of Kuwait" since 1961.

## History

Following the post-glacial flooding of the [Persian Gulf basin](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persian_Gulf "Persian Gulf"), debris from the [Tigris–Euphrates river](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tigris%E2%80%93Euphrates_river_system "Tigris–Euphrates river system") formed a substantial delta, creating most of the land in present-day Kuwait and establishing the present coastlines.[^29] One of the earliest evidence of human presence dates back to the [Mesolithic](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mesolithic "Mesolithic") era (c. 8000 BC).[^30] Historically, most of present-day Kuwait was part of ancient [Mesopotamia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mesopotamia "Mesopotamia").[^31] [^32]

During the [Ubaid period](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ubaid_period "Ubaid period") (c. 5500–3700 BC), Kuwait was the central borderland between Mesopotamia and Eastern Arabia,[^33] [^34] [^35] [^36] [^37] including [Bahra 1](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bahra_1 "Bahra 1") and [site H3](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/H3_\(Kuwait\) "H3 (Kuwait)") in [Subiya](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Subiya,_Kuwait "Subiya, Kuwait").[^33] [^38] [^39] [^40] [^41] One of the world's earliest [reed boats](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Reed_boats "Reed boats") was discovered at [site H3](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/H3_\(Kuwait\) "H3 (Kuwait)") dating back to the Ubaid period.[^42] Other Neolithic sites are located in Khiran and [Sulaibikhat](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sulaibikhat "Sulaibikhat").[^33]

[Mesopotamians](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mesopotamian "Mesopotamian") first settled in the Kuwaiti island of [Failaka](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Failaka_Island "Failaka Island") in 2000 BC.[^43] [^44] Traders from the [Sumerian](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sumer "Sumer") city of [Ur](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ur "Ur") inhabited Failaka and ran a mercantile business.[^43] [^44] The island had many Mesopotamian-style buildings typical of those found in [Iraq](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Iraq "Iraq") dating from around 2000 BC.[^44] [^43] In 4000 BC until 2000 BC, Kuwait was home to the [Dilmun civilization](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Dilmun_civilization "Dilmun civilization").[^45] [^46] [^47] [^48] [^30] Dilmun included Al-Shadadiya,[^30] [Akkaz](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Akkaz_Island "Akkaz Island"),[^45] [Umm an Namil](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Umm_an_Namil_Island "Umm an Namil Island"),[^45] [^49] and [Failaka](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Failaka_Island "Failaka Island").[^45] [^48] At its peak in 2000 BC, Dilmun controlled the [Persian Gulf](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persian_Gulf "Persian Gulf") trading routes.[^50]

Following the [Fall of Babylon](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fall_of_Babylon "Fall of Babylon"), the bay of Kuwait came under the control of the [Achaemenid Empire](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Achaemenid_Empire "Achaemenid Empire") (c. 550‒330 BC) as the bay was repopulated after seven centuries of abandonment.[^51] Failaka was under the control of the Achaemenid Empire as evidenced by the archaeological discovery of Achaemenid strata.[^52] [^53] There are [Aramaic](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Aramaic "Aramaic") inscriptions that testify Achaemenid presence.[^53]

In fourth century BC, the [ancient Greeks](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ancient_Greeks "Ancient Greeks") colonized the bay of Kuwait under [Alexander the Great](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Alexander_the_Great "Alexander the Great"). The ancient Greeks named mainland Kuwait *Larissa* and Failaka was named *[Ikaros](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ikaros_\(Failaka_Island\) "Ikaros (Failaka Island)")*.[^54] [^55] [^56] [^57] The bay of Kuwait was named *Hieros Kolpos*.[^58] According to [Strabo](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Strabo "Strabo") and [Arrian](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arrian "Arrian"), Alexander the Great named Failaka *Ikaros* because it resembled the [Aegean Island](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Aegean_island "Aegean island") of that name in size and shape. Elements of [Greek mythology](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Greek_mythology "Greek mythology") were mixed with the local cults.[^59] "Ikaros" was also the name of a prominent city situated in Failaka.[^60] Large [Hellenistic](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hellenistic "Hellenistic") [forts](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Towns_of_ancient_Greece#Military_settlements "Towns of ancient Greece") and [Greek temples](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Greek_temple "Greek temple") were uncovered.[^61] Archaeological remains of Greek colonization were also discovered in Akkaz, Umm an Namil, and Subiya.[^30]

![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/94/Seleucid_Empire_alternative_map.jpg/250px-Seleucid_Empire_alternative_map.jpg)

The Seleucid Empire at its greatest extent

At the time of Alexander the Great, the mouth of the [Euphrates River](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Euphrates "Euphrates") was located in northern Kuwait.[^62] [^63] The Euphrates river flowed directly into the Persian Gulf via Khor [Subiya](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Subiya,_Kuwait "Subiya, Kuwait") which was a river channel at the time.[^62] [^63] Failaka was located 15 kilometers from the mouth of the Euphrates river.[^62] [^63] By the first century BC, the Khor Subiya river channel dried out completely.[^62] [^63]

In 127 BC, Kuwait was part of the [Parthian Empire](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Parthian_Empire "Parthian Empire") and the kingdom of [Characene](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Characene "Characene") was established around [Teredon](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Teredon "Teredon") in present-day Kuwait.[^64] [^65] [^66] Characene was centered in the region encompassing southern Mesopotamia,[^67] Characene coins were discovered in Akkaz, Umm an Namil, and Failaka.[^68] [^69] A busy Parthian commercial station was situated in Kuwait.[^70]

In 224 AD, Kuwait became part of the [Sassanid Empire](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sassanid_Empire "Sassanid Empire"). At the time of the Sassanid Empire, Kuwait was known as *Meshan*,[^71] which was an alternative name of the kingdom of Characene.[^72] [^73] Akkaz was a [Partho](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Parthian_Empire "Parthian Empire") - [Sassanian](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sassanian "Sassanian") site;[^74] the [Sassanid religion](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Zoroastrianism "Zoroastrianism") 's [tower of silence](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tower_of_silence "Tower of silence") was discovered in northern Akkaz.[^74] [^75] [^76] Late Sassanian settlements were discovered in Failaka.[^77] In [Bubiyan](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bubiyan_Island "Bubiyan Island"), there is archaeological evidence of Sassanian to early Islamic periods of human presence as evidenced by the recent discovery of torpedo-jar pottery shards on several prominent beach ridges.[^78]

in 1669 AD, Kuwait became under Bani Khalid Emirate (Arabic: إِمَارَةُ بَنِي خَالِدٍ) or the Emirate of Al Humaid from the Bani Khalid tribe was a state that arose in the eastern region of the Arabian Peninsula in 1669 after Emir Barrak ibn Ghurayr made his capital in [Al-Mubarraz](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Al-Mubarraz "Al-Mubarraz") in [Alahsa](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Al-Ahsa_Oasis "Al-Ahsa Oasis"), then managed to defeat the [Ottoman Empire](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ottoman_Empire "Ottoman Empire") represented by [Lahsa Eyalet](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lahsa_Eyalet "Lahsa Eyalet") and drove them out of the region. in 1752 after the death of Sulayman bin Muhammad Al Khalidi, the Utub Tribe Elected [Sabah Bin Jaber The First](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sabah_bin_Jaber "Sabah bin Jaber") to rule Kuwait and declare independence from the Emirate of Bani Khalid. [ar](https://ar.wikipedia.org/wiki/%D8%A7%D9%84%D9%83%D9%88%D9%8A%D8%AA)

### 1752–1945: Pre-oil

![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/83/MarinetimeMKuwaitAlshami.jpg/250px-MarinetimeMKuwaitAlshami.jpg)

Marine Museum in Kuwait City. Demonstrates the founding of Kuwait as a sea port for merchants.

In the early to mid 1700s, [Kuwait City](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kuwait_City "Kuwait City") was a small [fishing village](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fishing_village "Fishing village"). Administratively, it was a sheikhdom, ruled by [sheikhs](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sheikh "Sheikh") from the local [Bani Khalid](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bani_Khalid "Bani Khalid") clan.[^79] Sometime in the mid-1700s, the [Bani Utbah](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bani_Utbah "Bani Utbah") settled in Kuwait City.[^80] [^81] Sometime after the death of the Bani Khalid's leader Barak bin Abdul Mohsen and the fall of the [Bani Khalid Emirate](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bani_Khalid_Emirate "Bani Khalid Emirate"), the Utub were able to wrest control of Kuwait as a result of successive [matrimonial alliances](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marriage_of_state "Marriage of state").[^81]

In the latter half of the eighteenth century, Kuwait began establishing itself as a maritime [port](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Port "Port") and gradually became a principal commercial center for the transit of goods between [Baghdad](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Baghdad "Baghdad"), India, Persia, [Muscat](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Muscat "Muscat"), and the [Arabian Peninsula](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arabian_Peninsula "Arabian Peninsula").[^82] [^83] By the late-1700s, Kuwait had established itself as a trading route from the Persian Gulf to [Aleppo](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Aleppo "Aleppo").[^84] During the [Persian siege of Basra in 1775–79](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ottoman%E2%80%93Persian_War_\(1775%E2%80%931776\) "Ottoman–Persian War (1775–1776)"), Iraqi merchants took refuge in Kuwait and were partly instrumental in the expansion of Kuwait's boatbuilding and trading activities.[^85] As a result, Kuwait's maritime commerce boomed,[^85] as the Indian trade routes with Baghdad, Aleppo, [Smyrna](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Smyrna "Smyrna") and [Constantinople](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Constantinople "Constantinople") were diverted to Kuwait during this time.[^84] [^86] [^87] The [East India Company](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/East_India_Company "East India Company") was diverted to Kuwait in 1792.[^88] The East India Company secured the sea routes between Kuwait, India and the east coasts of Africa.[^88] After the Persians withdrew from [Basra](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Basra "Basra") in 1779, Kuwait continued to attract trade away from Basra.[^89] The flight of many of Basra's leading merchants to Kuwait continued to play a significant role in Basra's commercial stagnation well into the 1850s.[^89]

The instability in Basra helped foster economic prosperity in Kuwait.[^90] [^91] In the late 18th century, Kuwait was a haven for Basra merchants fleeing [Ottoman](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ottoman_government "Ottoman government") persecution.[^92] Kuwait was the center of [boat building](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Boat_building "Boat building") in the Persian Gulf,[^93] its ships renowned throughout the [Indian Ocean](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Indian_Ocean "Indian Ocean").[^94] [^95] Its sailors developed a positive reputation in the Persian Gulf.[^82] [^96] [^97] In the 19th century, Kuwait became significant in the [horse trade](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Horse_trading "Horse trading"),[^98] with regular shipments in sailing vessels.[^98] In the mid 19th century, it was estimated that Kuwait exported an average of 800 horses to India annually.[^90]

In 1899, ruler Sheikh [Mubarak Al Sabah](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mubarak_Al-Sabah "Mubarak Al-Sabah") signed an agreement with the [British government in India](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Presidencies_and_provinces_of_British_India "Presidencies and provinces of British India") (subsequently known as the [Anglo-Kuwaiti Agreement of 1899](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Anglo-Kuwaiti_Agreement_of_1899 "Anglo-Kuwaiti Agreement of 1899")) making Kuwait a [British protectorate](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/British_protectorate "British protectorate"). This gave Britain exclusive access and trade with Kuwait, while denying Ottoman and Germany provinces to the north a port on the Persian Gulf. The [Sheikhdom of Kuwait](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sheikhdom_of_Kuwait "Sheikhdom of Kuwait") remained a British protectorate until 1961.[^79] [^99]

![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ac/Basra_Province_1897.png/250px-Basra_Province_1897.png)

The Basra Vilayet of the Ottoman Empire in 1897. After the Anglo-Ottoman Convention of 1913, Kuwait was established as an autonomous kaza, or district, of the Ottoman Empire and a de facto protectorate of Great Britain. 100

After the [Anglo-Ottoman Convention of 1913](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Anglo-Ottoman_Convention_of_1913 "Anglo-Ottoman Convention of 1913"), Kuwait was established as an autonomous *[kaza](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kaza "Kaza"),* or district, of the Ottoman Empire and a *[de facto](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/De_facto "De facto")* protectorate of Great Britain.

During [World War I](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/World_War_I "World War I"), the [British Empire](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/British_Empire "British Empire") imposed a trade blockade against Kuwait because its ruler at the time, [Salim Al-Mubarak Al-Sabah](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Salim_Al-Mubarak_Al-Sabah "Salim Al-Mubarak Al-Sabah"), supported the [Ottoman Empire](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ottoman_Empire "Ottoman Empire").[^101] [^102] [^103] The British economic blockade heavily damaged Kuwait's economy.[^103]

In 1919, Sheikh [Salim Al-Mubarak Al-Sabah](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Salim_Al-Mubarak_Al-Sabah "Salim Al-Mubarak Al-Sabah") intended to build a commercial city in the south of Kuwait. This caused a diplomatic crisis with Najd, but Britain intervened, discouraging Sheikh Salim. In 1920, an attempt by the [Ikhwan](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ikhwan "Ikhwan") to build a stronghold in southern Kuwait led to the [Battle of Hamdh](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Battle_of_Hamdh "Battle of Hamdh"). The Battle of Hamdh involved 2,000 [Ikhwan](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ikhwan "Ikhwan") fighters against 100 Kuwaiti [cavalrymen](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cavalrymen "Cavalrymen") and 200 Kuwaiti [infantrymen](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Infantrymen "Infantrymen"). The battle lasted for six days and resulted in heavy but unknown casualties on both sides resulting in the victory of the Ikhwan forces and leading to the battle of Jahra around the Kuwait Red Fort. The [Battle of Jahra](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Battle_of_Jahra "Battle of Jahra") happened as the result of the [Battle of Hamdh](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Battle_of_Hamdh "Battle of Hamdh"). A force of three to four thousand [Ikhwan](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ikhwan "Ikhwan"), led by [Faisal Al-Dawish](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Faisal_Al-Dawish "Faisal Al-Dawish"), attacked the [Red Fort](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kuwait_Red_Fort "Kuwait Red Fort") at Al-Jahra, defended by fifteen hundred men. The fort was besieged and the Kuwaiti position precarious.[^104] The Ikhwan attack repulsed for the while, negotiations began between Salim and Al-Dawish; the latter threatened another attack if the Kuwaiti forces did not surrender. The local merchant class convinced Salim to call in help from British troops, who showed up with airplanes and three warships, ending the attacks.[^104] [^105] After the Battle of Jahra, Ibn Saud's warriors, the [Ikhwan](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ikhwan "Ikhwan"), demanded that Kuwait follows five rules.[^106] They demanded that all the [Shias](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Shias "Shias") be evicted, that all should adopt the [Ikhwan doctrine](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wahhabism "Wahhabism"), that the Turks be labelled " [heretics](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Heretics "Heretics") ", that smoking, [munkar](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Munkar_and_Nakir "Munkar and Nakir"), and prostitution be abolished, and that American missionary hospital be destroyed.[^107]

![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/91/Jahra-castle.jpg/250px-Jahra-castle.jpg)

The Kuwait Red Fort in Al Jahra

The [Kuwait–Najd War](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kuwait%E2%80%93Najd_War "Kuwait–Najd War") of 1919–20 erupted in the [aftermath of World War I](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Aftermath_of_World_War_I "Aftermath of World War I"). The war occurred because [Ibn Saud](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ibn_Saud "Ibn Saud") of Najd wanted to annex Kuwait.[^101] [^108] The sharpened conflict between Kuwait and Najd led to the death of hundreds of Kuwaitis. The war resulted in sporadic border clashes throughout 1919–1920.

When [Percy Cox](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Percy_Cox "Percy Cox") was informed of the border clashes in Kuwait, he sent a letter to the [Ruler of Arabistan](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Emirate_of_Arabistan "Emirate of Arabistan") Sheikh [Khazʽal Ibn Jabir](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Khaz%CA%BDal_Ibn_Jabir "Khazʽal Ibn Jabir") offering the Kuwaiti throne to either him or one of his heirs. Khaz'al refused.[^109] He then asked:

> ...even so, do you think that you have come to me with something new? Al Mubarak's position as ruler of Kuwait means that I am the true ruler of Kuwait. So there is no difference between myself and them, for they are like the dearest of my children and you are aware of this. Had someone else come to me with this offer, I would have complained about them to you. So how do you come to me with this offer when you are well aware that myself and Al Mubarak are one soul and one house, what affects them affects me, whether good or evil.[^109]

Following the Kuwait–Najd War in 1919–20, Ibn Saud imposed a trade blockade against Kuwait from the years 1923 until 1937.[^110] The goal of the Saudi economic and military attacks on Kuwait was to annex as much of Kuwait's territory as possible. At the [Uqair conference](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Uqair_Protocol_of_1922 "Uqair Protocol of 1922") in 1922, the boundaries of Kuwait and Najd were set; as a result of British interference, Kuwait had no representative at the Uqair conference. After the Uqair conference, Kuwait was still subjected to a Saudi economic blockade and intermittent Saudi [raiding](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Raid_\(military\) "Raid (military)").

Kuwait immensely declined in regional economic importance,[^95] due to the trade blockades and the world economic depression.[^101] Before [Mary Bruins Allison](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mary_Bruins_Allison "Mary Bruins Allison") visited Kuwait in 1934, Kuwait had already lost its prominence in long-distance trade.[^95]

![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/16/Kuwait1944.jpg/330px-Kuwait1944.jpg)

Celebration at Seif Palace in 1944

The [Great Depression](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Great_Depression "Great Depression") harmed Kuwait's economy, starting in the late 1920s.[^110] International trading was one of Kuwait's main sources of income before oil.[^110] Kuwait's merchants were mostly intermediary merchants.[^110] As a result of the decline of European demand for goods from India and Africa, Kuwait's economy suffered. The decline in international trade resulted in an increase in gold smuggling by Kuwait's ships to India.[^110] Some local merchant families became rich from this smuggling.[^111] Kuwait's [pearl](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pearl "Pearl") industry also collapsed as a result of the worldwide economic depression.[^111] At its height, Kuwait's pearl industry had led the world's luxury market, regularly sending out between 750 and 800 ships to meet the European elite's desire for pearls.[^111] During the economic depression, luxuries like pearls were in little demand.[^111] The Japanese invention of [cultured pearls](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cultured_pearl "Cultured pearl") also contributed to the collapse of Kuwait's pearl industry.[^111]

[Freya Stark](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Freya_Stark "Freya Stark") wrote about the extent of poverty in Kuwait at the time:[^110]

> Poverty has settled in Kuwait more heavily since my last visit five years ago, both by sea, where the pearl trade continues to decline, and by land, where the blockade established by Saudi Arabia now harms the merchants.

On 22 February 1938, [oil](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Petroleum "Petroleum") was first discovered in the [Burgan field](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Burgan_field "Burgan field").

### 1946–1980: State-building

Between 1946 and 1980, Kuwait experienced a period of prosperity driven by oil and its liberal cultural atmosphere; this period is called the "golden era of Kuwait".[^112] [^113] [^114] [^115] In 1946, crude oil was exported for the first time. In 1950, a major public-work programme began to enable Kuwaiti citizens to enjoy a luxurious standard of living.

By 1952, the country became the largest oil exporter in the Persian Gulf region. This massive growth attracted many foreign workers, especially from Palestine, Iran, India, and Egypt – with the latter being particularly political within the context of the [Arab Cold War](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arab_Cold_War "Arab Cold War").[^116] It was also in 1952 that the first masterplan of Kuwait was designed by the British planning firm of [Minoprio](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Anthony_Minoprio "Anthony Minoprio"), [Spenceley](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hugh_Spencely "Hugh Spencely"), and Macfarlane. In 1958, *[Al-Arabi](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Al-Arabi_\(magazine\) "Al-Arabi (magazine)")* magazine was first published.[^117] Many foreign writers moved to Kuwait because they enjoyed greater [freedom of expression](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Freedom_of_expression "Freedom of expression") than elsewhere in the Middle East.[^118] [^119] Kuwait's press was described as one of the [freest in the world](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Freedom_of_the_press "Freedom of the press").[^120] Kuwait was the pioneer of the post- [Nahda](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nahda "Nahda") literary renaissance in the Middle East.[^117]

In June 1961, Kuwait became independent with the end of the [British protectorate](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sheikhdom_of_Kuwait#History_as_a_Protected_State_of_Britain "Sheikhdom of Kuwait") and the Sheikh [Abdullah Al-Salim Al-Sabah](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Abdullah_Al-Salim_Al-Sabah "Abdullah Al-Salim Al-Sabah") became [Emir of Kuwait](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Emir_of_Kuwait "Emir of Kuwait"). Kuwait's [national day](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Public_holidays_in_Kuwait "Public holidays in Kuwait"), however, is celebrated on 25 February, the anniversary of the coronation of Sheikh Abdullah (it was originally celebrated on 19 June, the date of independence, but concerns over the summer heat caused the government to move it).[^121]

At the time, Kuwait was considered the most developed country in the region.[^122] [^123] [^124] Kuwait was the pioneer in the Middle East in diversifying its earnings away from oil exports.[^125] The [Kuwait Investment Authority](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kuwait_Investment_Authority "Kuwait Investment Authority") is the world's first sovereign wealth fund.

Kuwaiti society embraced liberal and non-traditional attitudes throughout the 1960s and 1970s.[^126] [^127] For example, most Kuwaiti women did not wear the [hijab](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hijab "Hijab") in the 1960s and 70s.[^128] [^129] At Kuwait University, [mini skirts](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mini_skirts "Mini skirts") were more common than the hijab among female Kuwaiti students.[^127]

![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4b/HMS_Victorious_%28R38%29_aerial_c1959.jpeg/250px-HMS_Victorious_%28R38%29_aerial_c1959.jpeg)

HMS Victorious taking part in Operation Vantage in July 1961

Although Kuwait formally gained independence in 1961, Iraq initially refused to recognize the country's independence by maintaining that Kuwait is part of Iraq, albeit Iraq later briefly backed down following a show of force by Britain and [Arab League](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arab_League "Arab League") support of Kuwait's independence.[^130] [^131] [^132]

The short-lived [Operation Vantage](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Operation_Vantage "Operation Vantage") crisis evolved in July 1961, as the Iraqi government threatened to invade Kuwait and the invasion was finally averted following plans by the Arab League to form an international Arab force against the potential Iraqi invasion of Kuwait.[^133] [^134] As a result of Operation Vantage, the Arab League took over the border security of Kuwait and the British had withdrawn their forces by 19 October.[^130] Iraqi prime minister [Abd al-Karim Qasim](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Abd_al-Karim_Qasim "Abd al-Karim Qasim") was killed in a coup in 1963 but, although Iraq recognised Kuwaiti independence and the military threat was perceived to be reduced, Britain continued to monitor the situation and kept forces available to protect Kuwait until 1971. There had been no Iraqi military action against Kuwait at the time: this was attributed to the political and military situation within Iraq which continued to be unstable.[^18]

A treaty of friendship between Iraq and Kuwait was signed in 1963 by which Iraq recognised the 1932 border of Kuwait.[^135] Under the terms of the newly drafted [Constitution](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Constitution_of_Kuwait "Constitution of Kuwait"), Kuwait held its first [parliamentary elections in 1963](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kuwaiti_parliamentary_election,_1963 "Kuwaiti parliamentary election, 1963").

![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b2/Gamal_Abdel_Nasser_with_Shaikh_Abdullah_III_Al-Salim_Al-Sabah.jpg/250px-Gamal_Abdel_Nasser_with_Shaikh_Abdullah_III_Al-Salim_Al-Sabah.jpg)

Abdullah Al-Salim Al-Sabah with Egyptian President Gamal Abdel Nasser during the Al-Sabah's visit to Cairo in 1962

[Kuwait University](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kuwait_University "Kuwait University") was established in 1966.[^124] Kuwait's [theatre industry](#Television_and_theatre) became well known throughout the region.[^112] [^124] After the 1967 [Six Day War](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Six_Day_War "Six Day War"), Kuwait along with other Arabic speaking countries voted the three no's of the [Khartoum Resolution](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Khartoum_Resolution "Khartoum Resolution"): no peace with Israel, no recognition of Israel, and no negotiations with Israel. From the 1970s onward, Kuwait scored highest of all Arab countries on the [Human Development Index](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human_Development_Index "Human Development Index").[^124] The Iraqi poet [Ahmed Matar](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ahmed_Matar "Ahmed Matar") left Iraq in the 1970s to take refuge in the more liberal environment of Kuwait. Kuwait is the 25th most peaceful country in the world, according to the 2024 [Global Peace Index](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Global_Peace_Index "Global Peace Index").[^136]

The [Kuwait-Iraq 1973 Samita border skirmish](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kuwait-Iraq_1973_Sanita_border_skirmish "Kuwait-Iraq 1973 Sanita border skirmish") evolved on 20 March 1973, when Iraqi army units occupied El-Samitah near the Kuwaiti border, which evoked an international crisis.[^137]

On 6 February 1974, [Palestinian militants occupied the Japanese embassy in Kuwait](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1974_attack_on_the_Japanese_Embassy_in_Kuwait "1974 attack on the Japanese Embassy in Kuwait"), taking the ambassador and ten others hostage. The militants' motive was to support the [Japanese Red Army](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Japanese_Red_Army "Japanese Red Army") members and Palestinian militants who were holding hostages on a Singaporean ferry in what is known as the [*Laju* incident](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Laju_incident "Laju incident"). Ultimately, the hostages were released, and the guerrillas allowed to fly to [Aden](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Aden "Aden"). This was the first time Palestinian guerrillas struck in Kuwait as the Al Sabah ruling family, headed by Sheikh Sabah Al-Salim Al-Sabah, funded the Palestinian resistance movement. Kuwait had been a regular endpoint for Palestinian [plane hijacking](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Aircraft_hijacking "Aircraft hijacking") in the past and had considered itself safe.

[Kuwait International Airport](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kuwait_International_Airport "Kuwait International Airport") was opened in 1979 by the Al Hani Construction with a joint venture of [Ballast Nedam](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ballast_Nedam "Ballast Nedam").

### 1981–1991: Wars and terrorism

The Al Sabah strongly advocated [Islamism](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Islamism "Islamism") throughout the 1980s.[^138] At that time, the most serious threat to the continuity of Al Sabah came from home-grown democrats,[^138] who were protesting the [1976 suspension of the parliament](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kuwaiti_general_election,_1975 "Kuwaiti general election, 1975").[^138] The Al Sabah were attracted to Islamists preaching the virtues of a [hierarchical](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hierarchical "Hierarchical") order that included loyalty to the Kuwaiti monarchy.[^138] In 1981, the Kuwaiti government [gerrymandered](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gerrymandered "Gerrymandered") electoral districts in favour of the Islamists.[^139] [^138] Islamists were the government's main allies, hence Islamists were able to dominate state agencies, such as the [government ministries](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Government_ministries "Government ministries").[^138]

![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/79/BrennendeOelquellenKuwait1991.jpg/250px-BrennendeOelquellenKuwait1991.jpg)

Kuwaiti oil fires set by retreating Iraqi forces in 1991

During the [Iran–Iraq War](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Iran%E2%80%93Iraq_War "Iran–Iraq War"), Kuwait ardently supported Iraq against Iran. As a result, there were [various pro-Iran terror attacks](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1983%E2%80%931988_Kuwait_terror_attacks "1983–1988 Kuwait terror attacks") across Kuwait, including the 1983 bombings, the attempted assassination of [Emir Jaber](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jaber_Al-Ahmad_Al-Sabah "Jaber Al-Ahmad Al-Sabah") in May 1985, the [1985 Kuwait City bombings](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1985_Kuwait_City_bombings "1985 Kuwait City bombings"), and the hijacking of several Kuwait Airways planes. Kuwait's economy and scientific research sector significantly suffered due to the pro-Iran terror attacks.[^140]

Simultaneously, Kuwait experienced a major [economic crisis](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Economic_crisis "Economic crisis") after the [Souk Al-Manakh stock market crash](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Souk_Al-Manakh_stock_market_crash "Souk Al-Manakh stock market crash") and [decrease in oil price](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1980s_oil_glut "1980s oil glut").[^141] [^142] [^143] [^144]

![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/93/Tankskuwait.jpg/250px-Tankskuwait.jpg)

Iraqi Armed Forces tanks in Kuwait City of Iraqi-occupied Kuwait on 2 August 1990 during the Iraqi invasion of Kuwait that began the Gulf War.

After the Iran–Iraq War ended, Kuwait declined an Iraqi request to forgive its US$65 billion debt.[^145] An economic rivalry between the two countries ensued after Kuwait increased its oil production by 40 percent.[^146] Tensions between the two countries increased further in July 1990, after Iraq complained to [OPEC](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/OPEC "OPEC") claiming that Kuwait was stealing its oil from a field near the border by [slant drilling](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Slant_drilling "Slant drilling") of the [Rumaila field](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Rumaila_field "Rumaila field").[^146]

In August 1990, Iraqi forces [invaded and annexed](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Invasion_of_Kuwait "Invasion of Kuwait") Kuwait without any warning. After a series of failed diplomatic negotiations, the United States led a coalition to remove the Iraqi forces from Kuwait, in what became known as the [Gulf War](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gulf_War "Gulf War"). On 26 February 1991, in phase of code-named [Operation Desert Storm](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Operation_Desert_Storm "Operation Desert Storm"), the coalition succeeded in driving out the Iraqi forces. As they retreated, Iraqi forces carried out a [scorched earth](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kuwaiti_oil_fires "Kuwaiti oil fires") policy by setting oil wells on fire.[^147]

During the Iraqi occupation, nearly 1,000 civilians were killed in Kuwait. In addition, 600 people went missing during Iraq's occupation;[^148] remains of approximately 375 were found in mass graves in Iraq. Kuwait celebrates 26 February as [Liberation Day](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Liberation_Day_\(Kuwait\) "Liberation Day (Kuwait)").

### 1992–2023: Post-war period

In the early 1990s, Kuwait [deported](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Palestinian_exodus_from_Kuwait_\(Gulf_War\) "Palestinian exodus from Kuwait (Gulf War)") nearly 400,000 Palestinians.[^149] Kuwait's policy was a form of [collective punishment](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Collective_punishment "Collective punishment"), in response to the alignment of the [PLO](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/PLO "PLO") with Saddam Hussein. Kuwait also deported thousands of Iraqis and Yemenis after the Gulf War.[^150] [^151] Hundreds of thousands of [stateless Bedoon](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bedoon "Bedoon"), also spelled Bidoon in UN documents, were also expelled from Kuwait in the early-to-mid 1990s.[^152] [^153] [^150] [^154] [^151] At the [House of Commons of the United Kingdom](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/House_of_Commons_of_the_United_Kingdom "House of Commons of the United Kingdom") in 1995, it was revealed that the Al Sabah ruling family deported 150,000 stateless Bedoon to refugee camps in the Kuwaiti desert near the Iraqi border with minimal water, insufficient food, and no basic shelter.[^155] [^153] Many of the stateless Bedoon fled to Iraq where they remain stateless people even today.[^156] [^157]

In March 2003, Kuwait became the springboard for the US-led [invasion of Iraq](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Invasion_of_Iraq "Invasion of Iraq"). In 2005, women won the right to vote and run in elections. Upon the death of the Emir Jaber in January 2006, Sheikh [Saad Al-Sabah](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Saad_Al-Sabah "Saad Al-Sabah") succeeded him but was removed nine days later due to his failing health. As a result, Sheikh [Sabah Al-Ahmad Al-Jaber Al-Sabah](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sabah_Al-Ahmad_Al-Jaber_Al-Sabah "Sabah Al-Ahmad Al-Jaber Al-Sabah") was sworn in as Emir. From that point onwards, Kuwait suffered from chronic political deadlock between the government and parliament which resulted in multiple cabinet reshuffles and dissolutions.[^158] This significantly hampered investment and economic reforms in Kuwait, making the country's economy much more dependent on oil.[^158]

Despite the political instability, Kuwait had the highest [Human Development Index](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human_Development_Index "Human Development Index") ranking in the Arab world from 2006 to 2009.[^159] [^160] [^161] [^162] [^163] [^164] China awarded Kuwait Investment Authority an additional $700 million quota on top of $300 million awarded in March 2012.[^165] The quota is the highest to be granted by China to foreign investment entities.[^165]

![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/6/65/Kuwait_Towers_in_night_time_by_%C2%A9lensofasif%2C_Kuwait_City.jpg/250px-Kuwait_Towers_in_night_time_by_%C2%A9lensofasif%2C_Kuwait_City.jpg)

Kuwait Towers

![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a3/%D8%B5%D9%88%D8%B1%D8%A9_%D8%AC%D9%88%D9%8A%D8%A9_%D9%84%D9%85%D8%A8%D9%86%D9%89_%D9%85%D8%AC%D9%84%D8%B3_%D8%A7%D9%84%D8%A7%D9%85%D8%A9.jpg/250px-%D8%B5%D9%88%D8%B1%D8%A9_%D8%AC%D9%88%D9%8A%D8%A9_%D9%84%D9%85%D8%A8%D9%86%D9%89_%D9%85%D8%AC%D9%84%D8%B3_%D8%A7%D9%84%D8%A7%D9%85%D8%A9.jpg)

Kuwait City nightscape, with the Kuwait National Assembly visible (illuminated white building in center)

In March 2014, [David S. Cohen](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/David_S._Cohen_\(attorney\) "David S. Cohen (attorney)"), who was then the United States [Secretary of the Treasury for Terrorism and Financial Intelligence](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Under_Secretary_of_the_Treasury_for_Terrorism_and_Financial_Intelligence "Under Secretary of the Treasury for Terrorism and Financial Intelligence"), and many others accused [Kuwait of funding terrorism](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kuwait_and_state-sponsored_terrorism "Kuwait and state-sponsored terrorism"), particularly for [ISIS](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/ISIS "ISIS") and [Al-Qaeda](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Al-Qaeda "Al-Qaeda").[^166] [^167] [^168] [^169] [^170] [^171] [^172] [^173] [^174] [^175]

On 26 June 2015, a [suicide bombing took place](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2015_Kuwait_mosque_bombing "2015 Kuwait mosque bombing") at a Shia Muslim mosque in Kuwait. The [Islamic State of Iraq and the Levant](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Islamic_State_of_Iraq_and_the_Levant "Islamic State of Iraq and the Levant") claimed responsibility for the attack. Twenty-seven people were killed and 227 people were wounded. It was the largest terror attack in Kuwait's history. In the aftermath, a lawsuit was filed accusing the Kuwaiti government of negligence and direct responsibility for the terror attack.[^176] [^177]

Due to [declining oil prices](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2010s_oil_glut "2010s oil glut") in the mid-to-late 2010s, Kuwait faced one of the worst economic crunches in its history.[^178] [Sabah Al Ahmad Sea City](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sabah_Al_Ahmad_Sea_City "Sabah Al Ahmad Sea City") was inaugurated in mid-2016.[^179] [^180] [^181] [^182] [^183] Simultaneously, Kuwait invested significantly in its economic relations with [China](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/China "China").[^184] At the time, China was Kuwait's largest trade partner.[^185] [^186] [^187] [^188] [^189]

Under the [Belt and Road Initiative](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Belt_and_Road_Initiative "Belt and Road Initiative"), Kuwait and China have various cooperation projects including [Al-Mutlaa](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Al-Mutlaa "Al-Mutlaa") which is currently under construction in northern Kuwait.[^190] [^191] [^192] [^193] [^194] The [Sheikh Jaber Al-Ahmad Al-Sabah Causeway](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sheikh_Jaber_Al-Ahmad_Al-Sabah_Causeway "Sheikh Jaber Al-Ahmad Al-Sabah Causeway") is part of the first phase of the [Silk City](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Madinat_al-Hareer "Madinat al-Hareer") project.[^195] The causeway was inaugurated in May 2019 as part of Kuwait Vision 2035,[^196] [^197] it connects Kuwait City to northern Kuwait.[^196] [^195]

The [COVID-19 pandemic](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/COVID-19_pandemic_in_Kuwait "COVID-19 pandemic in Kuwait") exacerbated Kuwait's economic crisis.[^198] [^199] [^200] [^201] Kuwait's economy faced a budget deficit of $46 billion in 2020.[^202] [^203] [^158] It was Kuwait's first fiscal deficit since 1995.[^204] [^205] In September 2020, Kuwait's Crown Prince Sheikh [Nawaf Al-Ahmad Al-Jaber Al-Sabah](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nawaf_Al-Ahmad_Al-Jaber_Al-Sabah "Nawaf Al-Ahmad Al-Jaber Al-Sabah") became the 16th Emir of Kuwait and the successor to Emir Sheikh Sabah Al-Ahmad Al-Jaber Al-Sabah, who died at the age of 91.[^206] In October 2020, Sheikh [Mishal Al-Ahmad Al-Jaber Al-Sabah](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mishal_Al-Ahmad_Al-Jaber_Al-Sabah "Mishal Al-Ahmad Al-Jaber Al-Sabah") was appointed as the Crown Prince.[^207] [^208] [^209] [^210] In December 2023, Kuwait's Emir Sheikh Nawaf al-Ahmad al-Jaber al-Sabah died and was replaced by Mishal Al-Ahmad Al-Jaber Al-Sabah*.*[^211]

### 2024–present: Citizenship revocations and 2026 Iran war

In early 2024, the Emir of Kuwait began [revoking the citizenship](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human_rights_in_Kuwait#Citizenship_revocation "Human rights in Kuwait") of many citizens (by decree).[^212] [^213] The National Assembly has been suspended since 10 May 2024.[^214] In March 2025, it was reported that the citizenship of 42,000 people was revoked in just six months.[^215] [^216] [^217] By December 2025, it was estimated that as many as 200,000 people have lost their Kuwaiti citizenship.[^218] According to *[Carnegie Endowment for International Peace](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Carnegie_Endowment_for_International_Peace "Carnegie Endowment for International Peace")*, Kuwait has weaponized citizenship revocation.[^219] It is one of the largest citizenship revocation policies to ever occur since the Second World War.[^220]

In January 2026, the United States government suspended immigrant visas for citizens of Kuwait and 74 other countries due to the high dependency of Kuwaiti immigrants on American welfare benefits.[^221] Kuwait is the only GCC country on the visa suspension list.[^221]

Kuwait has the largest US military presence in the entire Middle East region.[^222] The United States government utilizes Kuwait-based military bases as staging hubs, training ranges, and logistical support for regional and international military operations.[^222] The bases include Camp Arifjan, Camp Buehring, Ali Al-Salem Air Field, and the naval base Camp Patriot.[^222] There are reportedly over 14,000 US military personnel stationed in the country.[^222]

Between February and April 2026, [Kuwait was subject to a campaign of aerial attacks](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2026_Iranian_strikes_on_Kuwait "2026 Iranian strikes on Kuwait") during the wider [2026 Iran war](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2026_Iran_war "2026 Iran war"). Despite Kuwait's self-proclaimed 'neutrality', Iranian forces targeted critical infrastructure in the country, including [Kuwait International Airport](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kuwait_International_Airport "Kuwait International Airport"), the [PIFSS tower](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Public_Institution_for_Social_Security_Fund "Public Institution for Social Security Fund"), the Ministries Complex, oil refineries, and many desalination plants, causing significant structural damage and challenging the country's energy and water security.[^223] [^224] [^225]

## Geography

![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2e/Satellite_image_of_Kuwait_in_November_2001.jpg/250px-Satellite_image_of_Kuwait_in_November_2001.jpg)

A satellite image of Kuwait reveals its desert topography.

![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/85/Kuwait_pol_06.jpg/250px-Kuwait_pol_06.jpg)

Kuwait shares land borders with Iraq and Saudi Arabia, and maritime borders with Iraq, Saudi Arabia, and Iran.

Located at the head of the [Persian Gulf](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persian_Gulf "Persian Gulf") in the north-east corner of the [Arabian Peninsula](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arabian_Peninsula "Arabian Peninsula"), Kuwait is one of the smallest countries in the world in terms of land area. Kuwait lies between latitudes [28°](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/28th_parallel_north "28th parallel north") and [31° N](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/31st_parallel_north "31st parallel north"), and longitudes [46°](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/46th_meridian_east "46th meridian east") and [49° E](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/49th_meridian_east "49th meridian east"). Kuwait is generally low-lying, with the highest point being 306 m (1,004 ft) [above sea level](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Above_sea_level "Above sea level").[^18] [Mutla Ridge](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mutla_Ridge "Mutla Ridge") is the highest point in Kuwait.

Kuwait has [ten islands](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_islands_of_Kuwait "List of islands of Kuwait").[^226] With an area of 860 km <sup>2</sup> (330 mi <sup>2</sup>), the [Bubiyan](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bubiyan_Island "Bubiyan Island") is the largest island in Kuwait and is connected to the rest of the country by a 2,380-metre-long (7,808 ft) bridge.[^227] 0.6% of Kuwaiti land area is considered arable [^18] with sparse vegetation found along its 499-kilometre-long (310 mi) coastline.[^18] [Kuwait City](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kuwait_City "Kuwait City") is located on [Kuwait Bay](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kuwait_Bay "Kuwait Bay"), a natural deep-water harbor.

Kuwait's [Burgan field](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Burgan_field "Burgan field") has a total capacity of approximately 70 billion barrels (11 billion cubic metres) of proven oil reserves. During the 1991 [Kuwaiti oil fires](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kuwaiti_oil_fires "Kuwaiti oil fires"), more than 500 oil lakes were created covering a combined surface area of about 35.7 km <sup>2</sup> (133⁄4 mi <sup>2</sup>).[^228] The resulting [soil contamination](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Soil_contamination "Soil contamination") due to oil and soot accumulation had made eastern and south-eastern parts of Kuwait uninhabitable. Sand and oil residue had reduced large parts of the Kuwaiti desert to semi-asphalt surfaces.[^229] The oil spills during the [Gulf War](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gulf_War "Gulf War") also drastically affected Kuwait's marine resources.[^230]

### Climate

Due to Kuwait's proximity to Iraq and Iran, the winter season in Kuwait is colder than other coastal countries in the region (especially UAE, Qatar, and Bahrain).[^231] Kuwait is also less humid than other coastal countries in the region. The spring season in March is warm with occasional thunderstorms. The frequent winds from the northwest are cold in winter and hot in summer. Southeasterly damp winds spring up between July and October. Hot and dry south winds prevail in spring and early summer. The shamal, a northwesterly wind common during June and July, causes dramatic sandstorms.[^232] Summers in Kuwait are some of the hottest on earth. The highest recorded temperature was 54.0 °C (129.2 °F) at [Mitribah](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mitribah "Mitribah") on 21 July 2016, which is the highest temperature recorded in Asia.[^233] [^234]

Kuwait [emits a lot of carbon dioxide per person](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_countries_by_carbon_dioxide_emissions_per_capita "List of countries by carbon dioxide emissions per capita") compared to most other countries.[^235] In recent years, Kuwait has been regularly ranked among the world's highest countries in term of CO <sub>2</sub> per capita emissions.[^236] [^237] [^238]

### Nature reserves

At present, there are five [protected areas](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protected_areas "Protected areas") in Kuwait recognized by the [IUCN](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/International_Union_for_Conservation_of_Nature "International Union for Conservation of Nature"). In response to Kuwait becoming the [169th signatory](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_parties_to_the_Ramsar_Convention "List of parties to the Ramsar Convention") of the [Ramsar Convention](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ramsar_Convention "Ramsar Convention"), [Bubiyan Island](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bubiyan_Island "Bubiyan Island") 's Mubarak al-Kabeer reserve was designated as the country's first Wetland of International Importance.[^239] The 50,948 ha (125,900 acres) reserve consists of small lagoons and shallow [salt marshes](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Salt_marsh "Salt marsh") and is important as a stop-over for migrating birds on two migration routes.[^239] The reserve is home to the world's largest breeding colony of [crab-plover](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Crab-plover "Crab-plover").[^239]

### Biodiversity

Currently, [444 species of birds](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_birds_of_Kuwait "List of birds of Kuwait") have been recorded in Kuwait, 18 species of which breed in the country.[^240] The arfaj is the national flower of Kuwait.[^241] Due to its location at the head of the Persian Gulf near the mouth of the [Tigris–Euphrates river](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tigris%E2%80%93Euphrates_river_system "Tigris–Euphrates river system"), Kuwait is situated at the crossroads of many major bird migration routes and between two and three million birds pass each year.[^242] Kuwait's marine and littoral ecosystems contain the bulk of the country's biodiversity heritage.[^242] The marshes in northern Kuwait and Jahra have become increasingly important as a refuge for passage migrants.[^242]

Twenty eight species of mammal are found in Kuwait; animals such as gerboa, desert rabbits and [hedgehogs](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hedgehog "Hedgehog") are common in the desert.[^242] Large carnivores, such as the [wolf](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wolf "Wolf"), [caracal](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Caracal "Caracal") and [jackal](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jackal "Jackal"), are no longer present.[^242] Among the endangered mammalian species are the [red fox](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Red_fox "Red fox") and [wild cat](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wild_cat "Wild cat").[^242] Forty reptile species have been recorded although none are endemic to Kuwait.[^242]

Kuwait, Oman and Yemen are the only locations where the endangered [smoothtooth blacktip shark](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Smoothtooth_blacktip_shark "Smoothtooth blacktip shark") is confirmed as occurring.[^243]

Kuwaiti islands are important breeding areas for four species of [tern](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tern "Tern") and the [socotra cormorant](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Socotra_cormorant "Socotra cormorant").[^242] [Kubbar Island](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kubbar_Island "Kubbar Island") has been recognised an [Important Bird Area](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Important_Bird_Area "Important Bird Area") (IBA) by [BirdLife International](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/BirdLife_International "BirdLife International") because it supports a [breeding colony](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bird_colony "Bird colony") of [white-cheeked terns](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/White-cheeked_tern "White-cheeked tern").[^244]

### Water and sanitation

![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e1/Water_stress%2C_top_countries_%282022%29.svg/250px-Water_stress%2C_top_countries_%282022%29.svg.png)

Kuwait was the most water stressed country in the world in 2022.

Kuwait is part of the [Tigris–Euphrates river system](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tigris%E2%80%93Euphrates_river_system "Tigris–Euphrates river system") basin.[^245] [^246] [^247] [^248] [^249] [^250] Several Tigris–Euphrates [confluences](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Confluence "Confluence") form parts of the Kuwait–Iraq border.[^251] [Bubiyan Island](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bubiyan_Island "Bubiyan Island") is part of the [Shatt al-Arab](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Shatt_al-Arab "Shatt al-Arab") delta.[^78] Kuwait is partially part of the [Mesopotamian Marshes](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mesopotamian_Marshes "Mesopotamian Marshes").[^252] [^253] [^254] Kuwait does not currently have any permanent rivers within its territory. However, Kuwait does have several [wadis](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_wadis_of_Kuwait "List of wadis of Kuwait"), the most notable of which is [Wadi al-Batin](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wadi_al-Batin "Wadi al-Batin") which forms the border between Kuwait and Iraq.[^255] Kuwait also has several river-like marine channels around Bubiyan Island, most notably [Khawr Abd Allah](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Khawr_Abd_Allah "Khawr Abd Allah") which is now an [estuary](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Estuary "Estuary"), but once was the point where the [Shatt al-Arab](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Shatt_al-Arab "Shatt al-Arab") emptied into the Persian Gulf. Khawr Abd Allah is located in southern Iraq and northern Kuwait, the [Iraq-Kuwait border](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Iraq-Kuwait_border "Iraq-Kuwait border") divides the lower portion of the estuary, but adjacent to the port of [Umm Qasr](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Umm_Qasr "Umm Qasr") the estuary becomes wholly Iraqi. It forms the northeast coastline of Bubiyan Island and the north coastline of [Warbah Island](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Warbah_Island "Warbah Island").[^256]

Kuwait relies on water [desalination](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Desalination "Desalination") as a primary source of fresh water for drinking and domestic purposes.[^257] [^258] There are currently more than six desalination plants.[^258] Kuwait was the first country in the world to use desalination to supply water for large-scale domestic use. The history of desalination in Kuwait dates back to 1951 when the first distillation plant was commissioned.[^257]

In 1965, the Kuwaiti government commissioned the Swedish engineering company of VBB ([Sweco](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sweco "Sweco")) to develop and implement a plan for a modern [water-supply system](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Water-supply_system "Water-supply system") for Kuwait City. The company built [five groups of water towers](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kuwait_Water_Towers "Kuwait Water Towers"), thirty-one towers total, designed by its chief architect [Sune Lindström](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sune_Lindstr%C3%B6m "Sune Lindström"), called "the mushroom towers". For a sixth site, the Emir of Kuwait, Sheikh [Jaber Al-Ahmed](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jaber_al-Ahmad_al-Jaber_al-Sabah "Jaber al-Ahmad al-Jaber al-Sabah"), wanted a more spectacular design. This last group, known as [Kuwait Towers](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kuwait_Towers "Kuwait Towers"), consists of three towers, two of which also serve as water towers.[^259] Water from the desalination facility is pumped up to the tower. The thirty-three towers have a standard capacity of 102,000 cubic meters of water. "The Water Towers" (Kuwait Tower and the Kuwait Water Towers) were awarded the [Aga Khan Award for Architecture](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Aga_Khan_Award_for_Architecture "Aga Khan Award for Architecture") (1980 Cycle).[^260]

Kuwait's fresh water resources are limited to groundwater, desalinated seawater, and treated wastewater effluents.[^257] There are three major municipal wastewater treatment plants.[^257] Most water demand is currently satisfied through seawater desalination plants.[^257] [^258] Sewage disposal is handled by a national sewage network that covers 98% of facilities in the country.[^261]

## Government and politics

### Political system

Kuwait is an [emirate](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Emirate "Emirate").[^5] The [Emir](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Emir_of_Kuwait "Emir of Kuwait") is the head of state, he belongs to the [House of Sabah](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/House_of_Sabah "House of Sabah") ruling family. The political system consists of an [appointed government](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cabinet_of_Kuwait "Cabinet of Kuwait") and [judiciary](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Legal_system_of_Kuwait "Legal system of Kuwait"). The [Polity data series](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Polity_data_series "Polity data series") [^264] and [Economist](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/The_Economist "The Economist") [Democracy Index](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Democracy_Index "Democracy Index") [^265] both categorize Kuwait as an [autocracy](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Autocracy "Autocracy").

![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b7/Seifpalace.jpg/250px-Seifpalace.jpg)

The Seif Palace, the original seat of the Government of Kuwait

Executive power is exercised by the government. The Emir appoints the prime minister, who in turn chooses the [cabinet of ministers](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cabinet_of_Kuwait "Cabinet of Kuwait") comprising the government. In recent decades, numerous policies of the Kuwaiti government have been characterized as " [demographic engineering](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Demographic_engineering "Demographic engineering") ",[^219] especially in relation to Kuwait's [stateless Bedoon crisis](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bedoon#Kuwait "Bedoon") and the [history of naturalization](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kuwaiti_nationality_law#History_of_naturalization_in_Kuwait "Kuwaiti nationality law") in Kuwait.[^219]

The Emir appoints the judges. The [Constitution of Kuwait](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Constitution_of_Kuwait "Constitution of Kuwait") was promulgated in 1962.[^266] The Constitutional Court is charged with ruling on the conformity of laws and decrees with the constitution.

Legislative power is exercised by the Emir. It was formerly exercised by the [National Assembly](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/National_Assembly_\(Kuwait\) "National Assembly (Kuwait)"). As per article 107 of the [Kuwait constitution](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Constitution_of_Kuwait "Constitution of Kuwait"), the Emir has the power to dissolve the assembly and elections for a new assembly should be held within two months.[^267] The Emir has suspended various articles of the constitution on three occasions: 29 August 1976 under [Sheikh Sabah Al-Salim Al-Sabah](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sabah_Al-Salim_Al-Sabah "Sabah Al-Salim Al-Sabah"), 3 July 1986 under [Sheikh Jaber Al-Ahmed Al-Sabah](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jaber_Al-Ahmad_Al-Sabah "Jaber Al-Ahmad Al-Sabah"), and 10 May 2024 under [Sheikh Mishal Al-Ahmad Al-Jaber Al-Sabah](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mishal_Al-Ahmad_Al-Jaber_Al-Sabah "Mishal Al-Ahmad Al-Jaber Al-Sabah").[^5]

According to [International IDEA](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/International_Institute_for_Democracy_and_Electoral_Assistance "International Institute for Democracy and Electoral Assistance") ’s Global State of Democracy (GSoD) Indices and Democracy Tracker, Kuwait performs in the low to mid-range on overall democratic measures, with particular weaknesses in political representation, including credible elections, effective parliament and inclusive suffrage.[^268] [^269] [^270] [Freedom House](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Freedom_House "Freedom House") previously rated the country as "partly free" in the [Freedom in the World](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Freedom_in_the_World "Freedom in the World") survey.[^271] Kuwait was also previously described as " [anocratic](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Anocracy "Anocracy") ".[^272]

![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/7/7f/Kuwait_City_National_Assembly_Building_5.jpg/250px-Kuwait_City_National_Assembly_Building_5.jpg)

National Assembly (Kuwait)

Kuwait's political instability has significantly hampered the country's economic development and infrastructure.[^273] [^158] [^199] Kuwait is regularly characterized as being a " [rentier state](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Rentier_state "Rentier state") " in which the ruling family uses oil revenues to buy the political acquiescence of the citizenry; more than 70% of government spending consists of public sector salaries and subsidies.[^274] Kuwait has the highest public sector wage bill in the GCC region as public sector wages account for 12.4% of GDP.[^202]

Kuwaiti women are considered among the most emancipated women in the Middle East. In 2014 and 2015, Kuwait was ranked first among Arab countries in the [Global Gender Gap Report](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Global_Gender_Gap_Report "Global Gender Gap Report").[^275] [^276] [^277] In 2013, 53% of Kuwaiti women participated in the labor force,[^278] where they outnumber working Kuwaiti men,[^279] giving Kuwait the highest female citizen participation in the workforce of any GCC country.[^279] [^278] [^280] According to the [Social Progress Index](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Social_Progress_Index "Social Progress Index"), Kuwait ranks first in [social progress](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Social_Progress_Index "Social Progress Index") in the Arab world and Muslim world and second highest in the Middle East after Israel.[^281] However, women's political participation in Kuwait has been limited.[^282] Despite multiple prior attempts at granting [Kuwaiti women suffrage](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Women%27s_suffrage_in_Kuwait "Women's suffrage in Kuwait"), they were not permanently enfranchised until 2005.[^283]

### Al Sabah dynasty

![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/05/Prime_Minister_of_Bharat_Shri_Narendra_Damodardas_Modi_meets_with_Emir_of_Kuwait_Sheikh_Mishal_Al-Ahmad_Al-Jaber_Al-Sabah.jpg/250px-Prime_Minister_of_Bharat_Shri_Narendra_Damodardas_Modi_meets_with_Emir_of_Kuwait_Sheikh_Mishal_Al-Ahmad_Al-Jaber_Al-Sabah.jpg)

Kuwait's emir Sheikh Mishal with Prime Minister of India Narendra Modi in December 2024

The Al Sabah ruling family adhere to the [Maliki school](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Maliki_school "Maliki school") of Sunni Islam. Article 4 of the [Kuwait constitution](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Constitution_of_Kuwait "Constitution of Kuwait") stipulates that Kuwait is a hereditary emirate whose emir must be an heir of [Mubarak Al-Sabah](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mubarak_Al-Sabah "Mubarak Al-Sabah").[^267] Mubarak had four sons, but an informal pattern of alternation between the descendants of his sons [Jabir](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jaber_II_Al-Sabah "Jaber II Al-Sabah") and [Salem](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Salim_Al-Mubarak_Al-Sabah "Salim Al-Mubarak Al-Sabah") emerged since his death in 1915.[^284] This pattern of succession had one exception before 2006, when Sheikh [Sabah Al-Salim](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sabah_Al-Salim_Al-Sabah "Sabah Al-Salim Al-Sabah"), a son of Salem, was named crown prince to succeed his half-brother Sheikh [Abdullah Al-Salem](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Abdullah_Al-Salim_Al-Sabah "Abdullah Al-Salim Al-Sabah") as a consequence of infighting and lack of consensus within the ruling family council.[^284] The alternating system was resumed when Sheikh Sabah Al-Salim named Sheikh [Jaber Al-Ahmed](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jaber_Al-Ahmad_Al-Sabah "Jaber Al-Ahmad Al-Sabah") of the Jabir branch as his crown prince, eventually ruling as Emir for 29 years from 1977 to 2006.[^284] On 15 January 2006 Emir Sheikh Jaber Al-Ahmed died, and his crown prince, Sheikh [Saad Al-Abdullah](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Saad_Al-Salim_Al-Sabah "Saad Al-Salim Al-Sabah") of the Salem branch, was named Emir.[^285] On 23 January 2006 the National Assembly unanimously voted in favor of Sheikh Saad Al-Abdullah abdicating in favor of Sheikh [Sabah Al-Ahmed](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sabah_Al-Ahmad_Al-Jaber_Al-Sabah "Sabah Al-Ahmad Al-Jaber Al-Sabah"), citing his illness with a form of dementia.[^284] Instead of naming a successor from the Salem branch as per convention, Sheikh Sabah Al-Ahmed named his half-brother Sheikh [Nawaf Al-Ahmed](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nawaf_Al-Ahmad_Al-Jaber_Al-Sabah "Nawaf Al-Ahmad Al-Jaber Al-Sabah") as crown prince and his nephew Sheikh [Nasser Al-Mohammed](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nasser_Al-Mohammed_Al-Sabah "Nasser Al-Mohammed Al-Sabah") as prime minister.[^284] On 16 December 2023, Sheikh [Nawaf Al-Ahmed](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nawaf_Al-Ahmad_Al-Jaber_Al-Sabah "Nawaf Al-Ahmad Al-Jaber Al-Sabah") died, and Sheikh [Mishal Al-Ahmad Al-Jaber](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mishal_Al-Ahmad_Al-Jaber_Al-Sabah "Mishal Al-Ahmad Al-Jaber Al-Sabah") would be the successor.

Theoretically, Article 4 of the constitution stipulates that the incoming Emir's choice of crown prince needs to be approved by an absolute majority of the [National Assembly](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/National_Assembly_\(Kuwait\) "National Assembly (Kuwait)").[^267] If this approval is not achieved, the emir is constitutionally required to submit three alternative candidates for crown prince to the National Assembly.[^267] This process previously caused contenders for power to engage in alliance-building in the political scene, which had taken historically private feuding within the ruling family to the "public arena and the political realm".[^284]

### Foreign relations

![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/59/Secretary_Rubio_Meetgs_with_Kuwaiti_First_Deputy_Prime_Minister_and_Minister_of_Interior.jpg/250px-Secretary_Rubio_Meetgs_with_Kuwaiti_First_Deputy_Prime_Minister_and_Minister_of_Interior.jpg)

Kuwait's Deputy Prime Minister and Minister of Interior Sheikh Fahad with US Secretary of State Marco Rubio in October 2025

The foreign affairs of Kuwait are handled at the level of the [Ministry of Foreign Affairs](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ministry_of_Foreign_Affairs_\(Kuwait\) "Ministry of Foreign Affairs (Kuwait)"). The first foreign affairs department bureau was established in 1961. Kuwait became the 111th member state of the [United Nations](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_Nations "United Nations") in May 1963. It is a long-standing member of the [Arab League](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arab_League "Arab League") and [Gulf Cooperation Council](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gulf_Cooperation_Council "Gulf Cooperation Council").

Before the [Gulf War](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gulf_War "Gulf War"), Kuwait was the only "pro- [Soviet](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Soviet "Soviet") " state in the Persian Gulf region.[^286] Kuwait acted as a conduit for the Soviets to the other Arab states of the Persian Gulf, and Kuwait was used to demonstrate the benefits of a pro-Soviet stance.[^286] In July 1987, Kuwait refused to allow U.S. military bases in its territory.[^287] As a result of the [Gulf War](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gulf_War "Gulf War"), Kuwait's relations with the US have improved ([major non-NATO ally](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Major_non-NATO_ally "Major non-NATO ally")).

Kuwait currently has the largest US military presence in the entire Middle East region.[^222] The United States government utilizes Kuwait-based military bases as staging hubs, training ranges, and logistical support for regional and international military operations.[^222] The bases include Camp Arifjan, Camp Buehring, Ali Al-Salem Air Field, and the naval base Camp Patriot.[^222] There are reportedly over 14,000 US military personnel stationed in the country.[^222]

Kuwait is also a major ally of [ASEAN](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Association_of_Southeast_Asian_Nations "Association of Southeast Asian Nations") and enjoys a close economic relationship with China.[^288] [^289] [^290] [^291] Under the [Belt and Road Initiative](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Belt_and_Road_Initiative "Belt and Road Initiative"), Kuwait and China have many important cooperation projects including [Al-Mutlaa](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Al-Mutlaa "Al-Mutlaa") and [Mubarak Al Kabeer Port](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mubarak_Al_Kabeer_Port "Mubarak Al Kabeer Port").[^292] [^195] [^190] [^191] [^192] [^293]

### Military

![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/46/BMP-3_and_M1_Abrams_of_Kuwaiti_Land_Forces.jpg/250px-BMP-3_and_M1_Abrams_of_Kuwaiti_Land_Forces.jpg)

BMP-3 and M1 Abrams of the Kuwaiti Land Forces

The Kuwaiti armed forces consist of the [Land Forces](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kuwait_Army "Kuwait Army"), the [Air Force](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kuwait_Air_Force "Kuwait Air Force") (including the Air Defense Force), the [Navy](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kuwait_Navy "Kuwait Navy") (including the Coast Guard), the [National Guard](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kuwait_National_Guard "Kuwait National Guard"), and the Emiri Guard, with a total of 17,500 active personnel and 23,700 reservists. The Emiri Guard is tasked with the protection of the Emir of Kuwait. The National Guard remains independent of the regular armed forces command structure, subordinated directly to the Emir and the prime minister, and is involved in both internal security and external defense. The Coast Guard is part of the [Ministry of Interior](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ministry_of_Interior_\(Kuwait\) "Ministry of Interior (Kuwait)") while all of the other branches are part of the [Ministry of Defense](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ministry_of_Defense_\(Kuwait\) "Ministry of Defense (Kuwait)"), and the National Guard provides assistance to both agencies. Since 1991 the United States has been the country's main security partner, carrying out training exercises with its military, and Kuwait is also a participant in the Gulf Cooperation Council's [Peninsula Shield Force](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Peninsula_Shield_Force "Peninsula Shield Force"). The Kuwaiti military uses American, Russian, and western European equipment.[^294] [^295]

In 2017 Kuwait reintroduced mandatory military service for its male citizens, consisting of four months of training and eight months of service. Conscription was previously in effect from 1961 to 2001, though it was not fully enforced at that time.[^296] [^297] Kuwait was the only Gulf country to have had military conscription until 2014, when Qatar also implemented the policy.[^298]

When Saudi Arabia began its [intervention in the Yemeni civil war](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Saudi-led_intervention_in_the_Yemeni_civil_war "Saudi-led intervention in the Yemeni civil war") in early 2015, Kuwait joined the Saudi-led coalition. Kuwaiti forces provided an artillery battalion and 15 fighter jets, though their contribution to the operations in Yemen was limited.[^299] [^300]

### Legal system

Kuwait follows the [civil law system](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Civil_law_\(legal_system\) "Civil law (legal system)") modeled after the French legal system;[^301] [^302] [^303] Kuwait's legal system is largely secular.[^304] [^305] [^306] [^307] [Sharia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sharia "Sharia") law governs only [family law](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Family_law "Family law") for Muslim residents,[^305] [^308] while non-Muslims in Kuwait have a secular family law. For the application of [family law](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Family_law "Family law"), there are three separate court sections: [Sunni](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sunni_Islam "Sunni Islam") ([Maliki](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Maliki "Maliki")), [Shia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Shia_Islam "Shia Islam"), and [non-Muslim](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Dhimmi "Dhimmi"). According to the [United Nations](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_Nations "United Nations"), Kuwait's legal system is a mix of [English common law](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/English_law#Common_law "English law"), [French civil law](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Law_of_France "Law of France"), [Egyptian civil law](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Egyptian_Civil_Code "Egyptian Civil Code") and Islamic law.[^309]

The [court system](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Judiciary "Judiciary") in Kuwait is secular.[^310] [^311] Unlike other [Arab states of the Persian Gulf](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arab_states_of_the_Persian_Gulf "Arab states of the Persian Gulf"), Kuwait does not have Sharia courts.[^311] Sections of the civil court system administer family law.[^311] Kuwait has the most secular [commercial law](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Commercial_law "Commercial law") in the [Persian Gulf region](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arab_States_of_the_Persian_Gulf "Arab States of the Persian Gulf").[^312] The parliament criminalized alcohol consumption in 1983.[^313] Kuwait's [Code of Personal Status](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Code_of_Personal_Status_\(Kuwait\) "Code of Personal Status (Kuwait)") was promulgated in 1984.[^314]

### Administrative divisions

![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/06/Kuwait_governorates_english.png/250px-Kuwait_governorates_english.png)

Governorates of Kuwait

Kuwait is divided into [six governorates](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Governorates_of_Kuwait "Governorates of Kuwait"):

1. [Al Asimah Governorate](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Al_Asimah_Governorate_\(Kuwait\) "Al Asimah Governorate (Kuwait)") (or Capital Governorate)
2. [Hawalli Governorate](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hawalli_Governorate "Hawalli Governorate")
3. [Farwaniya Governorate](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Farwaniya_Governorate "Farwaniya Governorate")
4. [Mubarak Al-Kabeer Governorate](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mubarak_Al-Kabeer_Governorate "Mubarak Al-Kabeer Governorate")
5. [Ahmadi Governorate](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ahmadi_Governorate "Ahmadi Governorate")
6. [Jahra Governorate](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jahra_Governorate "Jahra Governorate")

The governorates are further [subdivided into Areas](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Areas_of_Kuwait "Areas of Kuwait").

### Human rights and corruption
