[Human rights in Kuwait](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human_rights_in_Kuwait "Human rights in Kuwait") has been the subject of significant criticism, particularly regarding the [Bedoon](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bedoon "Bedoon") (stateless people).[^154] [^152] [^315] [^150] The Kuwaiti government's handling of the stateless Bedoon crisis has come under criticism from many human rights organisations and even the [United Nations](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_Nations "United Nations").[^316] According to [Human Rights Watch](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human_Rights_Watch "Human Rights Watch") in 1995, Kuwait has produced 300,000 stateless Bedoon.[^317] Kuwait has the largest number of stateless people in the entire region.[^152] [^318] Since 1986, the Kuwaiti government has refused to grant any form of documentation to the Bedoon including birth certificates, death certificates, identity cards, marriage certificates, and driving licences.[^318] [^319] According to several human rights organizations, Kuwait is committing [ethnic cleansing](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ethnic_cleansing "Ethnic cleansing") and [genocide](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Genocide "Genocide") against the stateless Bedoon.[^154] [^152] [^318]

On the other hand, human rights organizations have criticized Kuwait for the human rights abuses toward foreign nationals. Foreign nationals account for 70% of Kuwait's total population. The [kafala system](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kafala_system "Kafala system") leaves foreign nationals prone to exploitation. Administrative deportation is very common in Kuwait for minor offenses, including minor traffic violations. Kuwait is one of the world's worst offenders in [human trafficking](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Trafficking_in_human_beings "Trafficking in human beings"). Hundreds of thousands of foreign nationals are subjected to numerous human rights abuses including involuntary servitude. They are subjected to physical and sexual abuse, non-payment of wages, poor work conditions, threats, confinement to the home, and withholding of passports to restrict their freedom of movement.[^320] [^321]

Kuwait's mistreatment of foreign workers has resulted in various high-profile diplomatic crises. In 2018, there was a [diplomatic crisis between Kuwait and the Philippines](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2018_Kuwait%E2%80%93Philippines_diplomatic_crisis "2018 Kuwait–Philippines diplomatic crisis") due to the mistreatment of Filipino workers in Kuwait. Approximately 60% of Filipinos in Kuwait are employed as domestic workers. In July 2018, Kuwaiti fashionista [Sondos Alqattan](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sondos_Alqattan "Sondos Alqattan") released a controversial video criticizing domestic workers from the Philippines.[^322] In 2020, there was a diplomatic crisis between Kuwait and Egypt due to the mistreatment of Egyptian workers in Kuwait.[^323]

Various Kuwaitis have been jailed after they criticized the Al Sabah ruling family.[^324] In 2010, the [U.S. State Department](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/U.S._State_Department "U.S. State Department") said it had concerns about the case of Kuwaiti blogger and journalist Mohammad Abdul-Kader al-Jassem who was on trial for allegedly criticizing the ruling al-Sabah family, and faced up to 18 years in prison if convicted.[^325] He was detained after a complaint against him was issued by the office of Kuwait's Emir Sheikh Sabah al-Ahmad al-Sabah.[^325]

Extensive corruption among Kuwait's high-level government officials is a serious problem resulting in tensions between the government and the public.[^326] In the [Corruption Perceptions Index](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Corruption_Perceptions_Index "Corruption Perceptions Index") 2007, Kuwait was ranked 60th out of 179 countries for corruption (least corrupt countries are at the top of the list). On a scale of 0 to 10 with 0 the most corrupt and 10 the most transparent, [Transparency International](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Transparency_International "Transparency International") rated Kuwait 4.3.[^327]

In 2009, 20% of the youth in juvenile centres had dyslexia, as compared to the 6% of the general population.[^328] Data from a 1993 study found that there is a higher rate of psychiatric morbidity in Kuwaiti prisons than in the general population.[^329] Additionally, [LGBTQ people in Kuwait](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/LGBTQ_rights_in_Kuwait "LGBTQ rights in Kuwait") have few legal protections.[^330]

## Economy

![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/4/42/Al_Hamra_Tower.jpg/250px-Al_Hamra_Tower.jpg)

Al Hamra Tower is the tallest sculpted tower in the world.

Kuwait has a wealthy [petroleum](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Petroleum "Petroleum") -based economy.[^331] Its official currency is the [Kuwaiti dinar](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kuwaiti_dinar "Kuwaiti dinar"). By various per-capita measures of economic output, Kuwait is one of the wealthiest countries in the world.[^332] [^333] [^334] [^335]

Since the end of the Gulf War, Kuwait's infrastructure projects market has regularly underperformed due to political deadlocks.[^336] [^158] In the early 2020s, it was reported that Kuwait was the region's most oil-dependent country with the weakest infrastructure quality and lowest share of economic diversification.[^158] [^199] [^337]

In 2019, Iraq was Kuwait's leading export market and food/agricultural products accounted for 94.2% of total export commodities.[^338] Globally, Kuwait's main export products were mineral fuels including oil (89.1% of total exports), aircraft and spacecraft (4.3%), organic chemicals (3.2%), plastics (1.2%), iron and steel (0.2%), gems and precious metals (0.1%), machinery including computers (0.1%), aluminum (0.1%), copper (0.1%), and salt, sulphur, stone and cement (0.1%).[^339] Kuwait was the world's biggest exporter of sulfonated, nitrated and nitrosated hydrocarbons in 2019.[^340] Kuwait was ranked 63rd out of 157 countries in the 2019 [Economic Complexity Index](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Economic_Complexity_Index "Economic Complexity Index") (ECI).[^340]

In recent decades, Kuwait has enacted certain measures to regulate foreign labor due to security concerns. For instance, workers from [Georgia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Georgia_\(country\) "Georgia (country)") are subject to heightened scrutiny when applying for entry visas, and an outright ban was imposed on the entry of domestic workers from [Guinea-Bissau](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Guinea-Bissau "Guinea-Bissau") and [Vietnam](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vietnam "Vietnam").[^341] Workers from [Bangladesh](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bangladesh "Bangladesh") are also banned.[^342] In April 2019, Kuwait added Ethiopia, Burkina Faso, Bhutan, Guinea and Guinea-Bissau to the list of banned countries bringing the total to 20. According to Migrant Rights, the bans are put in place mainly due to the fact that these countries lack embassies and labour corporations in Kuwait.[^343]

### Petroleum and natural gas

Despite its relatively small territory, Kuwait has proven crude [oil reserves](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_countries_by_proven_oil_reserves#Countries "List of countries by proven oil reserves") of 104 billion barrels, estimated to be 10% of the world's reserves. Kuwait also has substantial [natural gas reserves](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_countries_by_natural_gas_proven_reserves "List of countries by natural gas proven reserves"). All natural resources in the country are state property.

As part of Kuwait Vision 2035, Kuwait aims to position itself as a global hub for the petrochemical industry.[^344] [Al Zour Refinery](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Al_Zour_Refinery "Al Zour Refinery") is the largest refinery in the Middle East.[^345] [^346] [^347] It is Kuwait's largest environmentally friendly oil refinery,[^348] [^344] where this refers to the effect on the local environment as opposed to the global environmental impact of burning the resulting oil. This Al Zour Refinery is a Kuwait-China cooperation project under the [Belt and Road Initiative](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Belt_and_Road_Initiative "Belt and Road Initiative").[^349] Al Zour LNG Terminal is the Middle East's largest import terminal for [liquefied natural gas](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Liquefied_natural_gas "Liquefied natural gas").[^350] [^351] [^352] It is the world's largest capacity LNG storage and regasification green field project.[^353] [^354] The project has attracted investments worth US$3 billion.[^355] [^356] Other megaprojects include biofuel and clean fuels.[^357] [^358] On January 20, 2025, the [Kuwait Oil Company](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kuwait_Oil_Company "Kuwait Oil Company") announced a major hydrocarbon discovery at the Al Jlaiaa offshore field, which it sees as a significant milestone in the nation's energy sector. The development aligns with Kuwait's strategic plans to enhance its offshore exploration and production capabilities.[^359] [^360]

### Health

![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/81/New_Amiri_Hospital_%26_Amiri_Residences.jpg/250px-New_Amiri_Hospital_%26_Amiri_Residences.jpg)

Amiri Hospital in Kuwait

Kuwait has a state-funded healthcare system, which provides treatment without charge to Kuwaiti nationals. There are outpatient clinics in every residential area in Kuwait. A public insurance scheme exists to provide reduced cost healthcare to expatriates. Private healthcare providers also run medical facilities in the country, available to members of their insurance schemes. As part of Kuwait Vision 2035, many new hospitals recently opened.[^361] [^362] [^363] In the years leading up to the [COVID-19 pandemic](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/COVID-19_pandemic "COVID-19 pandemic"), Kuwait invested in its health care system at a rate that was proportionally higher than most other GCC countries.[^364] Under the Kuwait Vision 2035 healthcare strategy, the public hospital sector significantly increased its capacity.[^362] [^361] [^363] Many new hospitals recently opened, Kuwait currently has 20 public hospitals.[^365] [^362] [^361] [^363] The new Sheikh Jaber Al-Ahmad Hospital is the largest hospital in the Middle East.[^366] Kuwait also has 16 private hospitals.[^361]

Private sector hospitals in Kuwait offer multiple specialities. This trend is likely to grow further, especially in tapping opportunities to reduce treatments performed overseas and develop inbound medical tourism market by developing high end speciality hospitals.[^367]

### Transport

Kuwait has a modern network of highways. [Roadways](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Roads_in_Kuwait "Roads in Kuwait") extended 5,749 km (3,572 mi), of which 4,887 km (3,037 mi) is paved. There are more than two million passenger cars, and 500,000 commercial taxis, buses, and trucks in use. On major highways the maximum speed is 120 km/h (75 mph). Since there is no railway system in the country, most people travel by automobiles.

![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3d/%D9%85%D8%A8%D9%86%D9%89_%D8%A7%D9%84%D8%B1%D9%83%D8%A7%D8%A8_4_%D9%85%D8%B7%D8%A7%D8%B1_%D8%A7%D9%84%D9%83%D9%88%D9%8A%D8%AA_%D8%A7%D9%84%D8%AF%D9%88%D9%84%D9%8A.jpg/250px-%D9%85%D8%A8%D9%86%D9%89_%D8%A7%D9%84%D8%B1%D9%83%D8%A7%D8%A8_4_%D9%85%D8%B7%D8%A7%D8%B1_%D8%A7%D9%84%D9%83%D9%88%D9%8A%D8%AA_%D8%A7%D9%84%D8%AF%D9%88%D9%84%D9%8A.jpg)

Kuwait International Airport - Terminal 4

![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ac/Kuwait_highway.jpg/250px-Kuwait_highway.jpg)

A highway in Kuwait City

The country's public transportation network consists almost entirely of bus routes. The state owned Kuwait Public Transportation Company was established in 1962. It runs local bus routes across Kuwait as well as longer distance services to other Gulf states. The main private bus company is CityBus, which operates about 20 routes across the country. Another private bus company, Kuwait Gulf Link Public Transport Services, was started in 2006. It runs local bus routes across Kuwait and longer distance services to neighbouring countries.

The Kuwait Ports Public Authority manages and operates ports across Kuwait. The country's principal commercial seaports are [Shuwaikh](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Shuwaikh "Shuwaikh") and Shuaiba, which handled combined cargo of 753,334 TEU in 2006.[^368] Mina Al-Ahmadi is the largest port in the country.

There are two airports in Kuwait. [Kuwait International Airport](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kuwait_International_Airport "Kuwait International Airport") serves as the principal hub for international air travel. State-owned [Kuwait Airways](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kuwait_Airways "Kuwait Airways") is the largest airline in the country. A portion of the airport complex is designated as Al Mubarak Air Base, which contains the headquarters of the [Kuwait Air Force](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kuwait_Air_Force "Kuwait Air Force"), as well as the Kuwait Air Force Museum. In 2004, the first private airline of Kuwait, [Jazeera Airways](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jazeera_Airways "Jazeera Airways"), was launched. In 2005, the second private airline, [Wataniya Airways](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wataniya_Airways "Wataniya Airways") was founded.

As of May 2025, Kuwait International Airport is facing serious problems, as 14 international airlines have stopped flying to the airport. This is due to issues such as management problems, a weak economy, and tough competition from nearby airports. Fewer flights have led to fewer passengers, causing worries about the airport's future and its dwindling importance in the region.[^369]

### Education

![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/29/Khaldiya_Campus.JPG/250px-Khaldiya_Campus.JPG)

Kuwait University

The general education system consists of four levels: [kindergarten](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kindergarten "Kindergarten") (lasting for 2 years), [primary](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Primary_education "Primary education") (lasting for 5 years), [intermediate](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Middle_school "Middle school") (lasting for 4 years) and [secondary](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Secondary_education "Secondary education") (lasting for 3 years).[^370] Schooling at primary and intermediate level is compulsory for all students aged 6 – 14. All the levels of state education, including higher education, are free.[^371] The public education system is undergoing a revamp due to a project in conjunction with the [World Bank](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/World_Bank "World Bank").[^372] [^373] There are two public universities and 14 private universities.

### Finance

The [Kuwait Investment Authority](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kuwait_Investment_Authority "Kuwait Investment Authority") (KIA) is Kuwait's largest [sovereign wealth fund](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sovereign_wealth_fund "Sovereign wealth fund") specializing in foreign investment. The KIA is the world's oldest sovereign wealth fund. Since 1953, the Kuwaiti government has directed investments into Europe, the United States and the [Asia–Pacific](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Asia%E2%80%93Pacific "Asia–Pacific"). In 2021, the holdings were valued at around $700 billion in assets.[^374] [^375] It is the [3rd largest](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sovereign_wealth_fund#Largest_sovereign_wealth_funds "Sovereign wealth fund") sovereign wealth fund in the world.[^374] [^375]

Kuwait has a leading position in the financial industry in the GCC.[^376] The Emir has promoted the idea that Kuwait should focus its energies, in terms of economic development, on the financial industry.[^376] The historical preeminence of Kuwait (among the GCC monarchies) in finance dates back to the founding of the [National Bank of Kuwait](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/National_Bank_of_Kuwait "National Bank of Kuwait") in 1952.[^376] The bank was the first local publicly traded corporation in the GCC region.[^376] In the late 1970s and early 1980s, an alternative stock market, trading in shares of GCC companies, emerged in Kuwait, the [Souk Al-Manakh](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Souk_Al-Manakh_stock_market_crash "Souk Al-Manakh stock market crash").[^376] At its peak, its market capitalization was the third highest in the world, behind only the United States and Japan, and ahead of the United Kingdom and France.[^376]

Kuwait has a large wealth-management industry.[^376] Kuwaiti investment companies administer more assets than those of any other GCC country, save the much larger Saudi Arabia.[^376] The Kuwait Financial Centre, in a rough calculation, estimated that Kuwaiti firms accounted for over one-third of the total assets under management in the GCC.[^376]

The relative strength of Kuwait in the financial industry extends to its stock market.[^376] For many years, the total valuation of [all companies](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_companies_of_Kuwait "List of companies of Kuwait") listed on the [Kuwait Stock Exchange](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kuwait_Stock_Exchange "Kuwait Stock Exchange") far exceeded the value of those on any other GCC bourse, except Saudi Arabia.[^376] In 2011, financial and banking companies made up more than half of the market capitalization of the Kuwaiti bourse; among all the GCC states, the market capitalization of Kuwaiti financial-sector firms was, in total, behind only that of Saudi Arabia.[^376] In recent years, Kuwaiti investment companies have invested large percentages of their assets abroad, and their foreign assets have become substantially larger than their domestic assets.[^376]

Kuwait is a major source of foreign economic assistance to other states through the [Kuwait Fund for Arab Economic Development](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kuwait_Fund_for_Arab_Economic_Development "Kuwait Fund for Arab Economic Development"), an autonomous state institution created in 1961 on the pattern of international development agencies. In 1974, the fund's lending mandate was expanded to include all [developing countries](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Developing_countries "Developing countries") in the world.

![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ee/Central_bank_of_Kuwait.jpg/250px-Central_bank_of_Kuwait.jpg)

Central Bank of Kuwait

In the past five years, there has been a rise in [entrepreneurship](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Entrepreneurship "Entrepreneurship") and small business start-ups in Kuwait.[^377] [^378] The [informal sector](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Informal_sector "Informal sector") is also on the rise,[^379] mainly due to the popularity of Instagram businesses.[^380] [^381] [^382] In 2020, Kuwait ranked fourth in the MENA region in startup funding after the UAE, Egypt and Saudi Arabia.[^383]

### Other non-oil industries

The biggest non-oil industry is steel manufacturing.[^384] [^385] [^386] [^387] [^388] United Steel Industrial Company (KWT Steel) is Kuwait's main steel manufacturing company, which caters to all of Kuwait's domestic market demands (particularly construction).[^385] [^384] [^386] [^387] Kuwait is self-sufficient in steel.[^385] [^384] [^386] [^387]

In 2016, Kuwait's food self-sufficiency ratio was 49.5% in vegetables, 38.7% in meat, 12.4% in dairy, 24.9% in fruits, and 0.4% in cereals.[^389] 8.5% of Kuwait's entire territory consists of agricultural land, although arable land constitutes 0.6% of Kuwait's entire territory.[^390] [^391] Historically, Jahra was a predominantly agricultural area. There are currently various farms in Jahra.[^392]

Kuwait was ranked 73rd in the [Global Innovation Index](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Global_Innovation_Index "Global Innovation Index") in 2025.[^393] [^394] According to the [United States Patent and Trademark Office](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States_Patent_and_Trademark_Office "United States Patent and Trademark Office"), Kuwait registered 448 [patents](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Patents "Patents") as of 31 December 2015.[^395] [^396] [^397] [^398] In the early to mid 2010s, Kuwait produced the largest number of scientific publications and patents per capita in the region and registered the highest growth regionally.[^399] [^400] [^401] [^402] [^403] [^397]

Kuwait was the first country in the region to implement [5G](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/5G "5G") technology.[^404] Kuwait is among the world's leading markets in 5G penetration.[^404] [^405]

Tourism in Kuwait still remains very limited due to poor infrastructure and the alcohol ban. The annual "Hala Febrayer" festival somewhat attracts tourists from neighboring GCC countries,[^406] and includes a variety of events including music concerts, parades, and carnivals.[^406] [^407] [^408] The festival is a month-long commemoration of the [liberation of Kuwait](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Liberation_of_Kuwait "Liberation of Kuwait"), and runs from 1 to 28 February. [Liberation Day](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Liberation_Day "Liberation Day") itself is celebrated on 26 February.[^409]

![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d9/The_Palms_Beach_Hotel_%26_Spa_in_Kuwait.jpg/250px-The_Palms_Beach_Hotel_%26_Spa_in_Kuwait.jpg)

The Palms Beach Hotel & Spa in Kuwait

In 2020, Kuwait's domestic travel and tourism spending was $6.1 billion.[^410] The [WTTC](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/World_Travel_and_Tourism_Council "World Travel and Tourism Council") named Kuwait as one of the world's fastest-growing countries in travel and tourism [GDP](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/GDP "GDP") in 2019, with 11.6% year-on-year growth.[^410] In 2016, the tourism industry generated nearly $500 million in revenue.[^411] In 2015, tourism accounted for 1.5 percent of the GDP.[^412] [^413] [Sabah Al Ahmad Sea City](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sabah_Al_Ahmad_Sea_City "Sabah Al Ahmad Sea City") is one of Kuwait's biggest attractions.

The [Amiri Diwan](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Amiri_Diwan_of_Kuwait "Amiri Diwan of Kuwait") recently inaugurated the new [Kuwait National Cultural District](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kuwait_National_Cultural_District "Kuwait National Cultural District") (KNCD), which comprises [Sheikh Abdullah Al Salem Cultural Centre](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sheikh_Abdullah_Al_Salem_Cultural_Centre "Sheikh Abdullah Al Salem Cultural Centre"), [Sheikh Jaber Al Ahmad Cultural Centre](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sheikh_Jaber_Al_Ahmad_Cultural_Centre "Sheikh Jaber Al Ahmad Cultural Centre"), [Al Shaheed Park](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Al_Shaheed_Park "Al Shaheed Park"), and [Al Salam Palace](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Al_Salam_Palace_\(Kuwait\) "Al Salam Palace (Kuwait)").[^414] [^415] [^416] [^417] With a capital cost of more than US$1 billion, the project is one of the largest cultural investments in the world.[^415] The Kuwait National Cultural District is a member of the [Global Cultural Districts Network](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Global_Cultural_Districts_Network "Global Cultural Districts Network").[^418] Al Shaheed Park is the largest green roof project ever undertaken in the region.[^419]

Space and satellite programmes

![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/45/KSR-1_Rocket.jpg/120px-KSR-1_Rocket.jpg)

Prototype of the Kuwait Space Rocket

Kuwait has an emerging space industry which is largely driven by private sector initiatives.[^420] Seven years after the launch of the world's first communications satellite, [Telstar 1](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Telstar_1 "Telstar 1"), Kuwait in October 1969 inaugurated the first satellite ground station in the Middle East, "Um Alaish".[^421] The Um Alaish satellite station complex housed several satellite ground stations including Um Alaish 1 (1969), Um Alaish 2 (1977), and Um Alaish 3 (1981). It provided satellite communication services in Kuwait until 1990 when it was destroyed by the Iraqi armed forces during the Iraqi invasion of Kuwait.[^422] In 2019, Kuwait's Orbital Space established an amateur satellite ground station to provide free access to signals from satellites in orbit passing over Kuwait. The station was named Um Alaish 4 to continue the legacy of "Um Alaish" satellite station.[^423] Um Alaish 4 is a member of FUNcube distributed [ground station](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ground_station "Ground station") network [^424] and the Satellite Networked Open Ground Station project ([SatNOGS](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/SatNOGS "SatNOGS")).[^425]

Kuwait's Orbital Space in collaboration with the Space Challenges Program [^426] and [EnduroSat](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/EnduroSat "EnduroSat") [^427] introduced an international initiative called "Code in Space". The initiative allows students from around the world to send and execute their own code in space.[^428] The code is transmitted from a satellite ground station to a [cubesat](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/CubeSat "CubeSat") ([nanosatellite](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Small_satellite "Small satellite")) orbiting earth 500 km (310 mi) above sea level. The code is then executed by the satellite's onboard computer and tested under real space environment conditions. The nanosatellite is called "QMR-KWT" (Arabic: قمر الكويت) which means "Moon of Kuwait", translated from Arabic.[^429] QMR-KWT launched to space on 30 June 2021 [^430] on [SpaceX](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/SpaceX "SpaceX") [Falcon 9 Block 5](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Falcon_9_Block_5 "Falcon 9 Block 5") rocket and was part of the payload of a satellite carrier called ION SCV Dauntless David by D-Orbit.[^431] It was deployed into its final orbit ([Sun-synchronous orbit](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sun-synchronous_orbit "Sun-synchronous orbit")) on 16 July 2021.[^432] QMR-KWT is Kuwait's first satellite.[^430] [^433] [^429] Building on the achievements of QMR-KWT, Orbital Space launched QMR-KWT 2 as Kuwait's 3rd satellite on 28 December 2025 aboard a Soyuz-2.1b rocket from Vostochny Cosmodrome in Russia. Like its predecessor, QMR-KWT 2 mission emphasizes accessibility, allowing students and young engineers to interact with an operational spacecraft in orbit.[^434] [^435] [^436]

The [Kuwait Space Rocket](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kuwait_Space_Rocket "Kuwait Space Rocket") (KSR) is a Kuwaiti project to build and launch the first [suborbital](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Suborbital_spaceflight "Suborbital spaceflight") [liquid bi-propellant rocket](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Liquid-propellant_rocket "Liquid-propellant rocket") in [Arabia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arabia "Arabia").[^437] The project is divided into two phases with two separate vehicles: an initial testing phase with KSR-1 as a [test vehicle](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Test_article_\(aerospace\) "Test article (aerospace)") capable of reaching an altitude of 8 km (5.0 mi) and a more expansive suborbital test phase with the KSR-2 planned to fly to an altitude of 100 km (62 mi).[^438]

Kuwait's Orbital Space in collaboration with the [Kuwait Scientific Center](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kuwait_Scientific_Center "Kuwait Scientific Center") (TSCK) introduced for the first time in Kuwait the opportunity for students to send a science experiment to space. The objectives of this initiative was to allow students to learn about (a) how science space missions are done; (b) [microgravity](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Micro-g_environment "Micro-g environment") (weightlessness) environment; (c) how to do science like a real scientist. This opportunity was made possible through Orbital Space agreement with [DreamUp](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/DreamUp "DreamUp") PBC and [Nanoracks](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/NanoRacks "NanoRacks") LLC, which are collaborating with [NASA](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/NASA "NASA") under a Space Act Agreement.[^439] The students' experiment was named "Kuwait's Experiment: E.coli Consuming Carbon Dioxide to Combat Climate Change".[^440] [^441] The experiment was launched on [SpaceX CRS-21](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/SpaceX_CRS-21 "SpaceX CRS-21") (SpX-21) spaceflight to the [International Space Station](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/International_Space_Station "International Space Station") (ISS) on 6 December 2020. Astronaut [Shannon Walker](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Shannon_Walker "Shannon Walker") (member of the ISS [Expedition 64](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Expedition_64 "Expedition 64")) conducted the experiment on behalf of the students. In July 2021, Kuwait University announced that it is launching a national satellite project as part of state-led efforts to pioneer the country's sustainable space sector.[^442] [^443] KuwaitSat-1 was launched on 3 Jaunray 2023.[^444] In 2024, Kuwait Foundation for the Advancement of Sciences (KFAS) established the Kuwait National Space Research Center (KNSRC), providing a dedicated institutional platform for space research, policy, and international cooperation. KNSRC is located at Kuwait University.[^445] [^446]

## Demographics

![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ef/Kuwaityouth5020.jpg/250px-Kuwaityouth5020.jpg)

Kuwaiti youth celebrating Kuwait's independence and liberation, 2011

Kuwait's 2023 population was 4.82 million people, of which 1.53 million were Kuwaitis and 3.29 million expatriates.[^22]

### Ethnic groups

[Expatriates in Kuwait](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Expatriates_in_Kuwait "Expatriates in Kuwait") account for around 60% of Kuwait's total population. At the end of December 2018, 57.65% of Kuwait's total population were [Arabs](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arabs "Arabs") (including Arab expats).[^447] [Indians](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Indian_people "Indian people") and [Egyptians](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Egyptians "Egyptians") are the largest expat communities respectively.[^448] [^22]

### Religion

![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/6/61/Siddiqa_Fatima_Zahra_Mosque.jpg/250px-Siddiqa_Fatima_Zahra_Mosque.jpg)

Siddiqa Fatima Zahra Mosque in Kuwait

![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/58/Holy_Family_Cathedral_%28Kuwait%29.jpg/250px-Holy_Family_Cathedral_%28Kuwait%29.jpg)

Holy Family Co-Cathedral

Kuwait's official state religion is [Maliki](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Maliki_school "Maliki school") Sunni Islam. The [Al Sabah](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Al_Sabah "Al Sabah") ruling family adhere to the [Maliki school](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Maliki_school "Maliki school") of Sunni Islam. Most Kuwaiti citizens are Muslim; there is no official national census but it is estimated that 60%–70% are Sunni and 30%–40% are Shia.[^449] [^450] Kuwait also has a large community of expatriate [Christians](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Christians "Christians"), [Hindus](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hinduism "Hinduism"), [Buddhists](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Buddhism "Buddhism"), and [Sikhs](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sikhism "Sikhism").[^451] As of 2020, there are an estimated 837,585 Christians, comprising 17.93% of the population — the second largest religious group.[^447] Most Christians in Kuwait are from [Kerala](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kerala "Kerala") in India, namely [Malankara Orthodox](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Malankara_Orthodox_Syrian_Church "Malankara Orthodox Syrian Church"), [Mar Thoma](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mar_Thoma_Syrian_Church "Mar Thoma Syrian Church"), and [Roman Catholic](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Catholic_Church "Catholic Church"). The first Malankara Orthodox parish was St. Thomas Indian Orthodox Pazhayapally Ahmadi, established in 1934.[^452] Kuwait includes a [native Christian](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Christianity_in_Kuwait#Kuwaiti_Christians "Christianity in Kuwait") community, estimated to be composed of between 259 and 400 Kuwaiti citizens.[^453] Kuwait is the only [GCC country](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cooperation_Council_for_the_Arab_States_of_the_Gulf "Cooperation Council for the Arab States of the Gulf") besides Bahrain to have a local Christian population who hold citizenship. A small number of Kuwaiti citizens follow the [Baháʼí Faith](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bah%C3%A1%CA%BC%C3%AD_Faith "Baháʼí Faith").[^451] [^454]

### Languages

Kuwait's official language is [Modern Standard Arabic](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Modern_Standard_Arabic "Modern Standard Arabic"), but its everyday usage is limited to journalism and education. [Kuwaiti Arabic](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kuwaiti_Arabic "Kuwaiti Arabic") is the variant of Arabic used in everyday life.[^455] English is widely understood and often used as a business language. Besides English, French is taught as a third language for the students of the [humanities](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Humanities "Humanities") at schools, but for two years only. Kuwaiti Arabic is a variant of [Gulf Arabic](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gulf_Arabic "Gulf Arabic"), sharing similarities with the dialects of neighboring coastal areas in Eastern Arabia.[^456] Due to immigration during its pre-oil history as well as trade, Kuwaiti Arabic borrowed a lot of words from [Persian](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persian_language "Persian language"), [Indian languages](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Languages_of_India "Languages of India"), [Balochi language](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Balochi_language "Balochi language"), Turkish, English and Italian.[^457]

Due to historical immigration, [Kuwaiti Persian](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kuwaiti_Persian "Kuwaiti Persian") is used among [Ajam Kuwaitis](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/%27Ajam_of_Kuwait "'Ajam of Kuwait").[^458] [^459] The [Iranian](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Iranian_languages "Iranian languages") sub-dialects of [Larestani](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Larestani "Larestani"), Khonji, Bastaki and Gerashi also influenced the vocabulary of Kuwaiti Arabic.[^460] Most Shia Kuwaiti citizens are of Iranian ancestry.[^461] [^462] [^463] [^464] [^465] [^466]

## Culture

Kuwait is considered to be a pioneer in the region when it comes to the arts and popular culture.[^467] [^468] Kuwaiti [popular culture](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Popular_culture "Popular culture"), in the form of theatre, radio, music, and television soap opera, flourishes and is even exported to neighboring states.[^469] [^470] Within the [Arab states of the Persian Gulf](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arab_states_of_the_Persian_Gulf "Arab states of the Persian Gulf"), the culture of Kuwait is the closest to the culture of [Bahrain](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bahrain "Bahrain"); this is evident in the close association between the two states in theatrical productions and soap operas.[^471]

### Performing arts

![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Mubarkiya_play.jpg/250px-Mubarkiya_play.jpg)

A theatrical play titled "Fateh Masr" at Al Mubarikya school in the 1940s

Kuwait has the oldest [performing arts](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Performing_arts "Performing arts") industry in the Arabian Peninsula.[^472] Kuwait's television drama industry is the largest and most active Gulf Arab drama industry and annually produces a minimum of fifteen serials.[^473] [^474] [^475] Kuwait is the main production center of the Gulf television drama and comedy scene.[^474] Most Gulf television drama and comedy productions are filmed in Kuwait.[^474] [^476] [^477] Kuwaiti soap operas are the most-watched soap operas from the Gulf region.[^473] [^478] [^479] Soap operas are most popular during the time of [Ramadan](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ramadan "Ramadan"), when families gather to break their fast.[^480] Although usually performed in the [Kuwaiti dialect](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kuwaiti_Arabic "Kuwaiti Arabic"), they have been shown with success as far away as [Tunisia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tunisia "Tunisia").[^481] Kuwait is frequently dubbed the " [Hollywood](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hollywood,_Los_Angeles "Hollywood, Los Angeles") of the Gulf" due to the popularity of its television soap operas and theatre.[^482] [^483]

Kuwait is the main centre of [scenographic](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Scenography "Scenography") and [performing arts education](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Performing_arts_education "Performing arts education") in the GCC region.[^484] [^485] Many famous Middle Eastern actors and singers attribute their success to training in Kuwait.[^486] The Higher Institute of Theatrical Arts (HIDA) provides [higher education](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Higher_education "Higher education") in theatrical arts.[^485] The institute has several divisions and attracts theatrical students from all over the GCC region. Many actors have graduated from the institute, such as [Souad Abdullah](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Souad_Abdullah "Souad Abdullah"), Mohammed Khalifa, [Mansour Al-Mansour](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mansour_Al-Mansour "Mansour Al-Mansour"), along with a number of prominent critics such as [Ismail Fahd Ismail](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ismail_Fahd_Ismail "Ismail Fahd Ismail").

Kuwait is known for its home-grown tradition of [theatre](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Theatre "Theatre").[^487] [^488] [^489] Kuwait is the only country in the Gulf Arab region with a theatrical tradition.[^487] The theatrical movement in Kuwait constitutes a major part of the country's cultural life.[^490] Theatrical activities in Kuwait date back to the 1920s when the first spoken dramas were released.[^491] Theatre activities are still popular today.[^490]

Theatre in Kuwait is [subsidized](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Subsidized "Subsidized") by the government, previously by the Ministry of Social Affairs and now by the National Council for Culture, Arts, and Letters (NCCAL).[^492] Every urban district has a public theatre.[^493] The public theatre in [Salmiya](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Salmiya "Salmiya") is named after actor [Abdulhussain Abdulredha](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Abdulhussain_Abdulredha "Abdulhussain Abdulredha"). The annual Kuwait Theater Festival is the largest theatrical arts festival in Kuwait.

Kuwait is the birthplace of various popular musical genres, such as [sawt](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sawt_\(music\) "Sawt (music)") and [fijiri](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fijiri "Fijiri").[^494] [^495] Traditional Kuwaiti music is a reflection of the country's seafaring heritage,[^496] which was influenced by many diverse cultures.[^497] [^498] [^494] Kuwait is widely considered the centre of [traditional music](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Folk_music "Folk music") in the GCC region.[^494] Kuwaiti music has considerably influenced the music culture in other GCC countries.[^499] [^495] Kuwait pioneered [contemporary Khaliji music](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Khaliji_\(music\) "Khaliji (music)").[^500] [^501] [^502] Kuwaitis were the first commercial recording artists in the Gulf region.[^500] [^501] [^502] The first known Kuwaiti recordings were made between 1912 and 1915.[^503]

Kuwait is home to various [music festivals](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Music_festivals "Music festivals"), including the International Music Festival hosted by the National Council for Culture, Arts and Letters (NCCAL).[^504] [^505] The [Sheikh Jaber Al-Ahmad Cultural Centre](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sheikh_Jaber_Al-Ahmad_Cultural_Centre "Sheikh Jaber Al-Ahmad Cultural Centre") contains the largest opera house in the Middle East.[^506] Kuwait has several academic institutions specializing in university-level [music education](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Music_education "Music education").[^507] [^508] The Higher Institute of Musical Arts was established by the government to provide [bachelor's degrees](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bachelor%27s_degrees "Bachelor's degrees") in music.[^509] [^507] [^508] In addition, the College of Basic Education offers bachelor's degrees in music education.[^509] [^507] [^508] The Institute of Musical Studies offers music education qualifications equivalent to [secondary school](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Secondary_school "Secondary school").[^509] [^508] [^507]

Kuwait has a reputation for being the central music influence of the GCC countries.[^510] Over the last decade of satellite television stations, many Kuwaiti musicians have become household names in other Arab countries. For example, [Bashar Al Shatty](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bashar_Al_Shatty "Bashar Al Shatty") became famous due to *[Star Academy](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Star_Academy_\(Arabia\) "Star Academy (Arabia)")*. Contemporary Kuwaiti music is popular throughout the Arab world. [Nawal El Kuwaiti](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nawal_El_Kuwaiti "Nawal El Kuwaiti"), Nabeel Shoail and [Abdallah Al Rowaished](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Abdallah_Al_Rowaished "Abdallah Al Rowaished") are the most popular contemporary performers.[^511]

### Visual arts

![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ae/Marriage%2C_Paris_-_UNESCO_-_PHOTO0000004583_0001.tiff/lossy-page1-250px-Marriage%2C_Paris_-_UNESCO_-_PHOTO0000004583_0001.tiff.jpg)

Traditional Kuwaiti wedding dress in the 1970s

Kuwait has the oldest [modern arts](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Modern_arts "Modern arts") movement in the Arabian Peninsula.[^512] [^513] [^514] Beginning in 1936, Kuwait was the first Gulf Arab country to grant scholarships in the arts.[^512] The Kuwaiti artist [Mojeb al-Dousari](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mojeb_al-Dousari "Mojeb al-Dousari") was the earliest recognized [visual artist](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Visual_artist "Visual artist") in the Gulf Arab region.[^515] He is regarded as the founder of [portrait](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Portrait "Portrait") art in the region.[^516] The Sultan Gallery was the first professional Arab art gallery in the Gulf.[^517] [^518]

Kuwait is home to more than [30 art galleries](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Art_of_Kuwait#Art_galleries "Art of Kuwait").[^519] [^520] In recent years, Kuwait's contemporary art scene has boomed.[^521] [^522] [^523] [Khalifa Al-Qattan](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Khalifa_Al-Qattan "Khalifa Al-Qattan") was the first artist to hold a [solo exhibition](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Solo_exhibition "Solo exhibition") in Kuwait. He founded a new art theory in the early 1960s known as "circulism".[^524] [^525] Other notable Kuwaiti artists include [Sami Mohammad](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sami_Mohammad "Sami Mohammad"), [Thuraya Al-Baqsami](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Thuraya_Al-Baqsami "Thuraya Al-Baqsami") and [Suzan Bushnaq](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Suzan_Bushnaq "Suzan Bushnaq").

The government organizes various [arts festivals](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arts_festivals "Arts festivals"), including the [Al Qurain Cultural Festival](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Al_Qurain_Cultural_Festival "Al Qurain Cultural Festival") and Formative Arts Festival.[^526] [^527] [^528] The Kuwait International Biennial was inaugurated in 1967,[^529] more than 20 Arab and foreign countries have participated in the biennial.[^529] Prominent participants include [Layla Al-Attar](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Layla_Al-Attar "Layla Al-Attar"). In 2004, the Al Kharafi Biennial for Contemporary Arab Art was inaugurated.

### Cuisine

Kuwaiti cuisine is a fusion of [Arabian](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arabian_cuisine "Arabian cuisine"), [Iranian](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Iranian_cuisine "Iranian cuisine"), and [Mesopotamian](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mesopotamian_cuisine "Mesopotamian cuisine") cuisines. Kuwaiti cuisine is part of the [Eastern Arabian cuisine](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Eastern_Arabian_cuisine "Eastern Arabian cuisine"). A prominent dish in Kuwaiti cuisine is *[machboos](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Machboos "Machboos")*, a rice-based dish usually prepared with [basmati](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Basmati "Basmati") rice seasoned with spices, and chicken or mutton.

[Seafood](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Seafood "Seafood") is a significant part of the Kuwaiti diet, especially [fish](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fish "Fish").[^530] [Mutabbaq samak](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mutabbaq_samak "Mutabbaq samak") is a national dish in Kuwait. Other local favourites are *hamour* ([grouper](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Grouper "Grouper")), which is typically served grilled, fried, or with [biryani](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Biryani "Biryani") rice because of its texture and taste; *safi* ([rabbitfish](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Rabbitfish "Rabbitfish")); *maid* ([mulletfish](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mulletfish "Mulletfish")); and *sobaity* ([sea bream](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sea_bream "Sea bream")).

Kuwait's traditional [flatbread](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Flatbread "Flatbread") is called Iranian *khubz*. It is a large flatbread baked in a special oven and it is often topped with sesame seeds. Numerous local bakeries dot the country; the bakers are mainly Iranians (hence the name of the bread, "Iranian *khubuz* ").

### Museums

![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/93/Jacckuwait.jpg/250px-Jacckuwait.jpg)

Sheikh Jaber Al-Ahmad Cultural Centre

![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/93/Al-Hashemi-II_%28ship%29.jpg/250px-Al-Hashemi-II_%28ship%29.jpg)

The Al-Hashemi-II, the largest wooden dhow ever built

The new [Kuwait National Cultural District](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kuwait_National_Cultural_District "Kuwait National Cultural District") (KNCD) consists of various cultural venues including [Sheikh Abdullah Al Salem Cultural Centre](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sheikh_Abdullah_Al_Salem_Cultural_Centre "Sheikh Abdullah Al Salem Cultural Centre"), [Sheikh Jaber Al Ahmad Cultural Centre](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sheikh_Jaber_Al_Ahmad_Cultural_Centre "Sheikh Jaber Al Ahmad Cultural Centre"), [Al Shaheed Park](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Al_Shaheed_Park "Al Shaheed Park"), and [Al Salam Palace](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Al_Salam_Palace_\(Kuwait\) "Al Salam Palace (Kuwait)").[^415] [^414] With a capital cost of more than US$1 billion, it is one of the largest cultural districts in the world.[^415] The Abdullah Salem Cultural Centre is the largest museum complex in the Middle East.[^531] [^532] The Kuwait National Cultural District is a member of the [Global Cultural Districts Network](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Global_Cultural_Districts_Network "Global Cultural Districts Network").[^418]

[Sadu House](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sadu_House "Sadu House") is among Kuwait's most important cultural institutions. [Bait Al-Othman](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bait_Al-Othman_Museum "Bait Al-Othman Museum") is the largest museum specializing in Kuwait's history. [The Scientific Center](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kuwait_Scientific_Center "Kuwait Scientific Center") is one of the largest science museums in the Middle East. The [Museum of Modern Art](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Museum_of_Modern_Art_\(Kuwait\) "Museum of Modern Art (Kuwait)") showcases the history of modern art in Kuwait and the region.[^533] The Kuwait Maritime Museum presents the country's maritime heritage in the pre-oil era. Several traditional Kuwaiti dhow ships are open to the public, such as [Fateh Al-Khayr](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fateh_Al-Khayr "Fateh Al-Khayr") and [Al-Hashemi-II](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Al-Hashemi-II "Al-Hashemi-II") which entered the [Guinness Book of World Records](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Guinness_Book_of_World_Records "Guinness Book of World Records") as the largest wooden dhow ever built.[^534] [^535] The [Historical, Vintage, and Classical Cars Museum](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Historical,_Vintage,_and_Classical_Cars_Museum "Historical, Vintage, and Classical Cars Museum") displays vintage cars from Kuwait's motoring heritage. The [National Museum](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kuwait_National_Museum "Kuwait National Museum"), established in 1983, has been described as "underused and overlooked".[^536]

Several Kuwaiti museums are devoted to [Islamic art](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Islamic_art "Islamic art"), most notably the [Tareq Rajab Museums](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tareq_Rajab_Museum "Tareq Rajab Museum") and [Dar al Athar al Islamiyyah](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Dar_al_Athar_al_Islamiyyah "Dar al Athar al Islamiyyah") cultural centres.[^537] [^538] [^539] [^540] The Dar al Athar al Islamiyyah cultural centres include education wings, conservation labs, and research libraries.[^540] [^541] There are several [art libraries](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Libraries "Libraries") in Kuwait.[^542] [^540] [^543] [^541] [Khalifa Al-Qattan](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Khalifa_Al-Qattan "Khalifa Al-Qattan") 's Mirror House is the most popular art museum in Kuwait.[^544] Many museums in Kuwait are private enterprises.[^545] [^538] In contrast to the top-down approach in other Gulf states, museum development in Kuwait reflects a greater sense of civic identity and demonstrates the strength of civil society in Kuwait, which has produced many independent cultural enterprises.[^546] [^538] [^545]

### Society

Urban Kuwaiti society is more [open](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Open_society "Open society") than other Gulf Arab societies.[^547] Kuwaiti citizens are ethnically diverse, consisting of both Arabs and [Persians (Ajam)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ajam_of_Kuwait "Ajam of Kuwait").[^548] [^549] [^550] Kuwait stands out in the region as the most liberal in empowering women in the public sphere.[^551] [^552] [^553] [Kuwaiti women](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Women_in_Kuwait "Women in Kuwait") outnumber men in the workforce.[^279] Kuwaiti political scientist Ghanim Alnajjar sees these qualities as a manifestation of Kuwaiti society as a whole, whereby in the Gulf Arab region it is "the least strict about traditions".[^554]

### Media

![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/0/0d/Kuwait_Liberation_Tower_cropped.jpg/250px-Kuwait_Liberation_Tower_cropped.jpg)

The 372 m (1,220 ft) tall Liberation Tower (left) is the main communication tower of Kuwait.

Kuwait produces more [newspapers and magazines](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_newspapers_in_Kuwait "List of newspapers in Kuwait") per capita than its neighbors.[^555] [^556] The state-owned [Kuwait News Agency](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kuwait_News_Agency "Kuwait News Agency") (KUNA) is the largest media house in the country. The Ministry of Information regulates the media industry in Kuwait. Kuwait's media is annually classified as partly free in the [Freedom of Press](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Freedom_of_Press "Freedom of Press") survey by Freedom House.[^557] Since 2005,[^558] Kuwait has frequently earned the highest ranking of all Arab countries in the annual [Press Freedom Index](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Press_Freedom_Index "Press Freedom Index") by Reporters Without Borders.[^559] [^560] [^561] [^562] [^563] [^564] [^565] [^566] [^567] In 2009, 2011, 2013 and 2014, Kuwait surpassed Israel as the country with the greatest press freedom in the Middle East.[^559] [^560] [^561] [^562] [^566] Kuwait is also frequently ranked as the Arab country with the greatest press freedom in Freedom House's annual Freedom of Press survey.[^568] [^569] [^570] [^571] [^572] [^573] [^574]

Kuwait has 15 satellite television channels, of which four are controlled by the Ministry of Information. State-owned [Kuwait Television](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kuwait_Television "Kuwait Television") (KTV) offered first colored broadcast in 1974 and operated five television channels. Government-funded Radio Kuwait also offers daily informative programming in several languages including [Arabic](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arabic_language "Arabic language"), [Persian](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persian_language "Persian language"), [Urdu](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Urdu "Urdu"), and English on the [AM](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/AM_broadcasting "AM broadcasting") and [SW](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Shortwave "Shortwave").

### Literature

Kuwait has in recent years produced several prominent contemporary writers such as [Ismail Fahd Ismail](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ismail_Fahd_Ismail "Ismail Fahd Ismail"), author of over twenty novels and numerous short story collections. There is also evidence that Kuwaiti literature has long been interactive with [English](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/English_literature "English literature") and [French literature](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/French_literature "French literature").[^575]

### Sport

![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dc/Kuwaiti_women.jpg/250px-Kuwaiti_women.jpg)

Kuwaiti women at a local football match

[Football](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Association_football "Association football") is the most popular sport in Kuwait. The [Kuwait Football Association](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kuwait_Football_Association "Kuwait Football Association") (KFA) is the governing body of football in Kuwait. The KFA organizes the [men's](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kuwait_national_football_team "Kuwait national football team"), [women's](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kuwait_women%27s_national_football_team "Kuwait women's national football team"), and [futsal](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Futsal "Futsal") national teams. The [Kuwaiti Premier League](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kuwaiti_Premier_League "Kuwaiti Premier League") is the top league of Kuwaiti football, featuring eighteen teams. The [Kuwait national football team](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kuwait_national_football_team "Kuwait national football team") have been the champions of the [1980 AFC Asian Cup](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1980_AFC_Asian_Cup "1980 AFC Asian Cup"), runners-up of the [1976 AFC Asian Cup](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1976_AFC_Asian_Cup "1976 AFC Asian Cup"), and have taken third place of the [1984 AFC Asian Cup](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1984_AFC_Asian_Cup "1984 AFC Asian Cup"). Kuwait has also been to one FIFA World Cup, in [1982](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1982_FIFA_World_Cup "1982 FIFA World Cup"); they drew 1–1 with [Czechoslovakia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Czechoslovakia_national_football_team "Czechoslovakia national football team") before losing to [France](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/France_national_football_team "France national football team") and [England](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/England_national_football_team "England national football team"), failing to advance from the first round. Kuwait is home to many football clubs including [Al-Arabi](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Al-Arabi_SC_\(Kuwait\) "Al-Arabi SC (Kuwait)"), [Al-Fahaheel](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fahaheel_\(football_club\) "Fahaheel (football club)"), [Al-Jahra](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Al_Jahra_\(football_club\) "Al Jahra (football club)"), [Al-Kuwait](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Al_Kuwait_Kaifan "Al Kuwait Kaifan"), [Al-Naser](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Al_Naser_Sporting_Club "Al Naser Sporting Club"), [Al-Salmiya](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Al_Salmiya_Club "Al Salmiya Club"), [Al-Shabab](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Al-Shabab_\(Kuwait\) "Al-Shabab (Kuwait)"), [Al Qadsia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Al_Qadsia_Kuwait "Al Qadsia Kuwait"), [Al-Yarmouk](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Al_Yarmouk_\(football_club\) "Al Yarmouk (football club)"), [Kazma](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Al_Kazma_Kuwait "Al Kazma Kuwait"), [Khaitan](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Khaitan "Khaitan"), [Sulaibikhat](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sulaibikhat "Sulaibikhat"), [Sahel](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sahel_\(Kuwaiti_football_club\) "Sahel (Kuwaiti football club)"), and [Tadamon](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tadamon,_Kuwait "Tadamon, Kuwait"). The biggest football rivalry in Kuwait is between [Al-Arabi](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Al-Arabi_SC_\(Kuwait\) "Al-Arabi SC (Kuwait)") and [Al Qadsia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Al_Qadsia_Kuwait "Al Qadsia Kuwait").

Basketball is one of the country's most popular sports. The [Kuwait national basketball team](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kuwait_national_basketball_team "Kuwait national basketball team") is governed by the Kuwait Basketball Association (KBA). Kuwait made its international debut in 1959. The national team has been to the [FIBA Asian Championship](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/FIBA_Asian_Championship "FIBA Asian Championship") in basketball eleven times. The [Kuwaiti Division I Basketball League](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kuwaiti_Division_I_Basketball_League "Kuwaiti Division I Basketball League") is the highest professional basketball league in Kuwait. [Cricket in Kuwait](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kuwait_national_cricket_team "Kuwait national cricket team") is governed by the [Kuwait Cricket Association](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kuwait_Cricket_Association "Kuwait Cricket Association"). Other growing sports include [rugby union](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Rugby_union_in_Kuwait "Rugby union in Kuwait"). [Handball](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kuwait_men%27s_national_handball_team "Kuwait men's national handball team") is widely considered to be the national icon of Kuwait, although football is more popular among the overall population.

![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/1/18/Jaber_Al-Ahmad_International_Stadium_2019_local.png/250px-Jaber_Al-Ahmad_International_Stadium_2019_local.png)

Jaber Al-Ahmad International Stadium

[Ice hockey in Kuwait](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kuwait_national_ice_hockey_team "Kuwait national ice hockey team") is governed by the [Kuwait Ice Hockey Association](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kuwait_Ice_Hockey_Association "Kuwait Ice Hockey Association"). Kuwait first joined the [International Ice Hockey Federation](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/International_Ice_Hockey_Federation "International Ice Hockey Federation") in 1985, but was expelled in 1992 due to a lack of ice hockey activity.[^576] Kuwait was re-admitted into the IIHF in May 2009.[^577] In 2015, Kuwait won the [IIHF Challenge Cup of Asia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/IIHF_Challenge_Cup_of_Asia "IIHF Challenge Cup of Asia").[^578] [^579]

In February 2020, Kuwait held for the first time a leg of the [UIM Aquabike World Championship](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Aquabike_World_Championship_\(powerboating\) "Aquabike World Championship (powerboating)") in front of Marina Beach City.[^580]
